Meow M

</question from>



<question>



Can you tell me your opinion about this short writing ?



Notice how she doesn't send you her thoughts in sound anymore?
Yes I do...
Notice how she does not send you written feelings anymore?
Yes I do...
What can you do about this?
A lot of things but the results will mean nothing.
What do you think?
I believe that this is how love is, it comes to you inevitably and without warning, it strikes the heart, conquers it, makes itself comfortable inside, sleeps well and when the morning light bothers its eyes leaves without a saying,  a note on the table or a good-bye kiss on the forehead while you sleep. Nothing sweet to leave behind just the dull loneliness and the silence of the room that you both used to sleep in, reminiscing on every single moment that at that time did not seem so special but now that you cannot experience them again you feel like screaming at the sky in hopes that it will scream an answer back or at least make the clouds mad and receive a lighting so that this pain and agony will perish.
What do you feel?
I cannot truly describe all of my feelings as they are deep inside and unreachable, the pure sight of my face can describe everything, the pose of my body, my staring at the floor and if you look deep into my eyes you would find yourself falling into a bottomless abysm where the dark is pitch black and the coldness hurts the bones, you will feel my torment and mourn with me as well, but I do not wish for you to feel what I feel.
So why do you love?
I do not love anymore, and for that I am about to perish, we have to love someone or at least something in order to keep living and keep going forward, love took us to where we are at the moment, if you did not love asking questions so much you would not be here at this moment asking them to me, and the answer to all of your questions should be "love", love or be loved, it does not matter, as long as love is present in your life your blood will be warm, your heart will keep pumping and your lungs will still drink the air outside, love, be loved or perish like me... 



</question>



<additional details>



Yes I am in love... but it hurts.



</additional details>

<question>



Rate this poem and star it if you like it.?



I wrote this poem in September of 1995, tell me what you think.



Tears of an Angel by Andrew D Hazell



Tears of an angel slowly fell to the ground
And when I saw them my life came crashing down
For I could not understand why she was so sad
An angels life, I thought, was never that bad
So I asked her why she cried these tears
And she said "I have seen your life in the upcoming years"
So I asked her would my life be so coy
And she said "They weren't tears of sadness but tears of joy"
"For your life will be full of content and happiness,"
"And you life wont be in such a mess."
So I asked about love would mine be so grand?
And she solemnly resonded "love and life don't go hand in hand"
I asked her what she meant by what she said,



Does this mean my love is dead?
But she spoke no words, just cried one tear.
Then said "That's for your love, have no fear."



</question>

<question>



Rate my poem and comment on what you liked or disliked please.?



BROKEN



Suffocation - heavy blanket
Lifeless - without emotion
Heart placed in my pocket
Escaping the commotion,



I can barely breathe
Two rings show corrosion
Overcome by seethe
Prepare for my explosion,



Marrow torn apart
And offspring show confusion
Not easy to depart
Nor - stay in this illusion,



No life to live - in somber
The end is now in sight
How long will it take?



With yet - another fight,



When will I find the courage?
To walk from being his wife
And find the love I dream of
With quality of life.



WRITTEN BY:
A.T – SILVERCHICK…..



</question>

</question from>



<question>



What is the difference between writing a poem and writing a song?



I love to write poetry and would like to write songs but i am not sure how the two connect if at all - please any info would be helpful, thank you.



</question>



<answer from>



spudcake
Member since: 05 November 2008
Total points: 139 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



A song is generally longer and more to the point. A song also has to have a melody.



</answer>



<answer from>



onyx-gol...
Member since: 20 May 2008
Total points: 1097 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



I write both poems and lyrics and find that with a song you will generally find that as the person above said it will be longer and more to the point but also have rhythm changes within the song so where a poems stanzas will generally be consistent and songs will not.  you also have to account for the type of music that the lyrics are going to go with after all there is no sense writing a song about flowers if you have death metal music going with it (although it would be an interesting combination I am sure.)  For me I tend to have a song in my head that I add lyrics to rather than have a poem in my head that i am adding music to.



</answer>



<answer from>



Eoredd
Member since: 20 November 2006
Total points: 28800 (Level 7)



</answer from>



<answer>



When you write a song, you think to adapt the words to a melody, to instruments and to human voice. It is quite different from writing a poem that is often meant to be read, not heard.



</answer>



<answer from>



Scantsan...
Member since: 25 September 2008
Total points: 466 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Poetry contains its own music.



</answer>

<question>



PLEASE RATE MY LOVE POEM!?



The season of Love



So are you the winter,
Are you frosty and cold,
No, you are not like winter, you are not frosty or cold,
You are not cold you glow in the gloom for all to see.



So if you are not Winter what are you?
Maybe you are Autumn,
Forever changing, forever loving,
And as the trees change do you change.



Or are you spring?
Just coming through the changing barriers,
Breaking out with rays of warmth and love,
But are you able to provide everlasting faith?



Maybe you're summer,
So warm and fun loving,
Not cold but hot and caring to everything,
But are you just season?



I do not know,



Could you be all four,
A bit of each season
Is this why i love you so.



</question>

All this wrong, Change it to this:



Are you the winter,
Frosty and cold,
No, you are not winter, not frosty or cold,
You are not cold you glow in the gloom for all to see.



So if you are not Winter what are you?
Maybe you are Autumn,
Forever changing, forever loving too,
And as the trees change i wonder do you?



Or are you spring?
Just coming through the changing barriers,
Breaking out with rays of warmth and love,
But are you able to provide everlasting faith?



Maybe you're summer,
So warm and fun loving,
Not cold but hot and caring to everything,
But are you just season?



I do not know,



Could you be all four,
A bit of each season
Is this why i love you more.



Put some music to that & I'd buy it!

<question>



This was inspired by another poet...any comments? And advice?



Memories
By Jonni F.



Your written word wakes up
some dormant corner of my mind.



Some casual phrase brings joy and love
rushing back to me,
like a freight train.



Reading on, the thoughts continue,
jumbled, racing through my soul.



Happy times,
when love was safe,
and the whole world was right.



The written memories that you share,
have given this to me.



</question>

<question>



I wrote a prayer poem for Obama. What do you think of it? Do you agree?



Let Us Pray,
Our Father,
who art in heaven,
hallowed be thy name.
Grant us the protection of your hand
from the danger across this land.
Give him the guidance that he should know
how to make this country grow.
Stay him not from giving peace
from our shores to the Middle East.
Touch his heart, our desperate plea
that he would not kill the unborn baby.
Let him know the marriage name
is for man and woman and not the same.
Please, dear God, for the life of our nation,
don't let us bring about alienation.
May he be your man among men
and let righteousness be his faith therein.
Now in the passing of the days
while the soul of the US prays,
Father, grant him the mind he shall need
and give him the ears when the people plead.



I fear him but I pray for him. I hope he is a good leader and takes in account all people. My prayers are for him.



</question>

Anyway, wonderful poem - very professional too!

<question>



Human Beings - A Poem I Wrote A While Back. Please Read On?



Okay just a little heads up, it's Lil Aurorette here. This is my new account 'cause the other one was kinda screwed and I've been trying to post this poem up for the 10th time. I'm not kidding. It just wouldn't show so I thought maybe changing accounts would solve the problem.



So anyway here's the poem:



I think human beings are weird.
I think human beings are bias.
I think human beings are petty.
I think human beings are ridiculous.



I know human beings are selfish.
I know human beings are heartless.
I know human beings are idiots.
I know human beings are cowards.



But then again.



I guess some human beings are nice.
I guess some human beings are kind.
I guess some human beings are sensible.
I guess some human beings are just.



I suppose some human beings are fair.
I suppose some human beings are pleasant.
I suppose some human beings are gracious.
I suppose some human beings are well-mannered.



But then again.



Human beings are disagreeable and I'm a human being.
So in conclusion, I disagree with what I've just written.



I honestly don't know what to think of it. What do you guys think?



</question>



<additional details>



to reply moon on clouds, I'm 14 soon to be 15, why?



anyway if you guys are interested, you guys can visit: http://rosesilhouette.webs.com/ for more of my poems.



</additional details>

Delicate Memories

<question from>



neonman
Member since: 26 June 2006
Total points: 20262 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</question from>



<question>



Can we...Yes we Can?  Can we...Yes we Can?



(hope is always the sweetest perfume on first night)



Can we…Yes we Can?



The Can Openers started peeling
Observing, taking notes.
Layer after layer of fiefdoms
all with their agendas.



With cc’s, cc’s and more cc’s
bees workdays always buzzed.
Agencies, special interests all,
hamster wheels were turning.



How many layers this government?
Who moves the wheels around?
The Can Openers were elected,



it’s their turn, pundits watch.



There’s efficiency in government!



Yes there is, surely is!
Just watch them cash their Friday paychecks,
Yes they can, yes they can!



Can Openers report… lengthy tomes
How to change, change to what?
Hydra moves wherever Hydra wants
bring the knights to battle!



Hope is coming, white horses are charging
Honeymoons- words so sweet
Yes we can…the new buzzed moniker
Yes we can?  Change is hope!

<question>



Rate this poem and star it if you like it.?



I wrote this poem in September of 1995, tell me what you think.



Tears of an Angel by Andrew D Hazell



Tears of an angel slowly fell to the ground
And when I saw them my life came crashing down
For I could not understand why she was so sad
An angels life, I thought, was never that bad
So I asked her why she cried these tears
And she said "I have seen your life in the upcoming years"
So I asked her would my life be so coy
And she said "They weren't tears of sadness but tears of joy"
"For your life will be full of content and happiness,"
"And you life wont be in such a mess."
So I asked about love would mine be so grand?
And she solemnly resonded "love and life don't go hand in hand"
I asked her what she meant by what she said,



Does this mean my love is dead?
But she spoke no words, just cried one tear.
Then said "That's for your love, have no fear."



</question>



<additional details>



Yes this does, for the most part, speak true today. Thanks for asking :D



</additional details>

<question from>



yousuf54
Member since: 24 March 2006
Total points: 161 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Poem analysis help! giving points...?



Nor dread nor hope attend
A dying animal;
A man awaits his end
Dreading and hoping all;
Many times he died,
Many times rose again.
A great man in his pride
Confronting murderous men
Casts derision upon
Supersession of breath;
He knows death to the bone --
Man has created death.



By: William Butler Yeats



Can anyone help analyze this poem, what do you think it means?



</question>



<answer from>



Rei
Member since: 27 August 2008
Total points: 347 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



it sounds like a man at war to me.



"confronting murderous men" - Enemies of the war
"a dying animal" - Animal is the man, has been struck and is dying
"Dreading and hoping all" - He Dreads he will die but hopes he will live
"Many times he died" - instead of dying, he lost all hope and predicted he would die.
"Many times he rose again" - Many times he lost all hope but regained his hope and continued to fight.
"He knows death to the bone -- Man has created death" - He could feel the death waiting for him.



The last line "man has created death" could mean two things in my opinion - He killed many in the war creating death / He himself was killed = created death.



it sounds silly but this is my opinion. I'm a drama/creative writing major at an art school.



</answer>



<asker's comment>



ty very helpful



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



HuuPoo
Member since: 14 October 2008
Total points: 615 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



Seems to refer to War, and representation of the soldier
Dying animal
a man awaits his end
dreading and hoping all
Many times he died
Many times rose again
A great man in his pride
confronting murderous men



</answer>

<question>



This was inspired by another poet...any comments? And advice?



Memories
By Jonni F.



Your written word wakes up
some dormant corner of my mind.



Some casual phrase brings joy and love
rushing back to me,
like a freight train.



Reading on, the thoughts continue,
jumbled, racing through my soul.



Happy times,
when love was safe,
and the whole world was right.



The written memories that you share,
have given this to me.

<answer>



Wish You Were Here.
Pink Floyd



So, so you think you can tell



Heaven from Hell,



Blue skys from pain.



Can you tell a green field



From a cold steel rail?



A smile from a veil?



Do you think you can tell?



And did they get you to trade



Your heros for ghosts?



Hot ashes for trees?



Hot air for a cool breeze?



Cold comfort for change?



And did you exchange



A walk on part in the war



For a lead role in a cage?



How I wish, how I wish you were here.



We're just two lost souls



Swimming in a fish bowl,



Year after year,



Running over the same old ground.



What have we found?



The same old fears.



Wish you were here.



</answer>

<question>



A women comes in my dream every night.....................?



A women comes in my dream every night,
i wish that i could hold her tight,
she makes me laugh
she makes me cry
sometimes i wonder why



her laughter reminds me of the morning temple bell
so calm, so serene, so peaceful. yeah i m mad crazy
about her, because she is very beautiful.
sometimes i see her cry,her tears remind of the melting snow
i kiss them and wipe them of her brow.



her face like morning sun is shining bright,
darkness melts away in front of her saintly light,
I love her teasing way, coming near me
and then running away.



i try to catch her, but alas night has ended, morning has come
just like dying person clings to his last breath, i cling to her memories througout the day,
night comes quickly that is alll i pray
waiting for the darkness and the night when she would come to
illuminate my life with her light.



</question>

<question>



WOW...A new prez...Do you remember...?



Here’s a nod to the White House resident
The one you voted to be your President
Congress holds the strings to the puppet
Make the Prez dance like a Henson Muppet
We’ll drill for oil wherever I please
I don’t give a **** about ancient trees
Cover my pals as we **** the environment
The bills due later but I need my retirement
I’ll leave the debt for ya’ll to pay
My future is right here today
You work forever to get your Lexus
I was born with the keys to Texas
Clinton goes down cause of spew on a collar
If only the dumb ***** would have chose to swalla’
Then there’s the legacy of the dead mans’ roster
What really went down with Brown and Foster
Papa Bush with his quotable quips
Looked in our eyes and said read my lips
Shipped the boys to war on foreign soil
What the **** you mean it isn’t about oil
You and Cheney’s **** musta’ been squirtin’
With all the mop up money from Haliburton
The Gipper couldn’t get out with a clean slate
Ollie fucked him with Iran and Contragate
Spineless **** with his back to the wall
The best line he could find is I don’t recall
And his silly *** wife with her just say no
With all the **** from D.C. we all needed mo’



</question>



<additional details>



Not much to say about the peanut farmer
Silly ****ing grin from a weak *** charmer
The press wouldn’t touch ole Jimmy Carter
But they sure loved to **** his precious daughter
Ford not around long to get a really good taste
But he sure made good fodder for Chevy Chase
He trusted his minions should have been a cynic
We can thank dear old Betty for giving us a clinic
Let’s reflect a moment on tricky Dick Nixon
His ducks in a row he had the fix in
A cast of misfits would seal his fate
He got screwed by the gang at Watergate
Let’s not forget the wonderful L.B.J.
We can thank him for killing J.F.K.
He took over what John had started
Left us with 50 thousand dearly departed



It’s no sin to be a Kennedy
Karma has its own remedy
There’s Teddy thinking with his dick
As Mary Jo goes down in Chappaquiddick
Thanks to the great JFK
Forever society will have to pay
Under the guise of equality
The civil wrongs act a hollow apology



Strange as it sounds there wasn’t a soul
Who could see anything from the grassy knoll
Congress brainwashed into submission
Sold us the saga of the Warren commission
Even Joe and Ethel’s’ magic wand
Couldn’t stop ole Sirhan Sirhan
I’ll stop now with one more note
Go ahead get out and vote
Look and see who’s on the ballot
Try and find one that fits your pallet
It doesn’t really matter they’re all the same
Greedy bastards caught up in the game
None of them have anything new to offer
Their only agenda is to fill their coffer
We’re no better today than we were then
It’s just the same old **** again
So remember when you make your choice

<answer>



Depression is an amazing thing if you can learn how to utilize it.  The poem is good, not great but a valiant effort that gets the point of your feelings across.  I am very familiar with this as a lot of my earlier writing was fueled by the same feelings and thoughts.  I was diagnosed with Manic Depression and was offered all kinds of anti depressants which I refused as i didn't want to lose that part of me, instead I wanted to control it myself and for the most part have done that (albeit with the help of friends and family sometimes).  Just remember that the darker the abyss is around you, the brighter the stars in your life become.



</answer>

<question>



Is This A Good Poem?  "Let's Hold Hands"?



There are days we all make mistakes
Nonw of was created to be perfect
But for some odd reason, we try so hard to be perfect
Instead of excepting the little mistakes we have had made
And owning up to our faults
We beat ourselves up, thinking "why God couldn't have made me better than this"
Instead of realizing that we all can learn from each other
We decided to bash and taunt each other
Betray one another turn our backs on one another
How about we reach our hand out to one another
And give a helping hand
Let God look down on us and smile
There is not one person walking this earth who is better than the other walking beside him
We are equal, because we were created by the ONE
And that is God
So lets hold hands
I'm speaking to everyone
Everyone of different race, ethnicity, color, characteristic, personality, attitude
dream, religion, and belief
Lets all hold hands and love each other for who we are
But not hate them for who they are not.



</question>

<answer>



After all the fun of growing your peppers, you just have to eat a few with this recipe. As with any recipe you can add more or less of any of the ingredients. You can also leave some out or add some of your own.



Ingredients:



4 Medium Green, Red, Orange or Yellow Peppers
1 lb Ground Beef or Pork
1/2 Cup Cooked Rice
1/2 Finely chopped onions
12 oz. Tomato Sauce or spaghetti sauce
1 tsp. salt



Optional: Add a little hot sauce to spice it up



Directions: Combine cooked ground beef and rice in frying pan add tomato sauce, onions and salt. Heat until sauce starts to boil (med heat)



Cut tops off Peppers and clean out the inside of the pepper. (Can also be cut vertically in half) Rinse peppers under cold water.



Stuff Peppers with meat and rice mixture. Put the top of the pepper back on and cook at 350 degrees for 35 min or until well baked on top.



Optional: With 5 minutes left on the timer sprinkle bread crumbs then place shredded mozzarella or cheddar cheese on top.



My wife made these last night and I swear to God, I ate them all.
Recipe for Stuffed Peppers Serves 4



</answer>

<answer>



I love you too babe.



My dearest Richard,



TD,



These words are aimed at me.



I Love him back.
I asked a lot of people to help me when I first met him.
They all said no. and all broke my confidence. No one said a word.



Even you said you couldn't be much help, you were having nothing to do with either your crazed Elys editor or him.
But you lie to me.
I can't make much sense of this.
Unless I tell a story.



A lady got a job, long needed for sanity.
Small town, to the people who live there,all knowing
small world for her unknowing.
She worked hard, the boss and her had many of the same friend.
All knew all, except her.
She worked and started to see the problems within her boss.
Not all jut little tiny things.
But the job was keeping her sane, out of the wells the darkness.
In one moment of promise to take the lead, grab the top position they headed out to final the sale, all in her hands.
In five minutes the lady found herself in the dark woods, alone and compromised. With pounding heart and al mseeing eyes.



Without being a bore I will spare you with the details .....
I skip now to two weeks later......
The lady saw the town's people and remarks where exchanged.
She asked, with widened eyes, "You mean you knew all this, and you did not tell me"?
The answer was "It is not for us to tell, we thought you should find out for yourself."



Dropping her jaw in disbelief, she died just a little......



She asked this time, first, not after. Not after falling in love.
Now you start like the ladies of the town...
You fecker! I trusted you! You fecker you broke me down.
RonnieXX



Source(s):



I hope this helped.



</answer>

<question>



Do you know what the Navajo greeting "Ya'ah'tee" means?



Saddled in leather
atop surefooted mule
the heat mixed my sweat
with the burdened beast's,
our nostrils flared in response



along rough, ragged base



of familiar red rock canyon
we haggardly made our way



to the ancient river bed
where my Navajo brother
on moccasined foot
offered an earnest "Ya'ah'tee"



our greeting of "it is good"



he saw my grey braids
eagle feathers adorned
beaded chest plate of color
his gift, in honor I wear
though red skin born I'm
not, still he calls me friend
my name, "Old Blue Eyes"



in dismount I yearn to



firmly plant both my feet
upon rich soil worked



and tilled with his



ancestors' blood



we warmly embrace
unashamed to acknowledge



a mutual respect, our undying



devotion to Mother Earth.



</question>

<question>



Are we all not glad that America has accepted CHANGE.? My love  4 change is boundless I am  a world's Anon, ?



incognito, citizen .



I like the best to win . I hate colour ,caste and creed and  consider Religion as personal. I  visit  churches, temples,monasteries, mosques and any such place ,to enjoy its silence and harmony and architecture.



Pease excuse me  for this Poetry, as I am no qualified poet, pseudo at best.THANK YOU.



LONG LIVE THE WORLD AND AMERICA



CHANGE ALONE IS PERMANENT



I recall Martin Luther King, some time long ago



He spoke ‘’I have a dream’’ so be it,



So must have Obama, the world needed the most indelible,



Also the only permanent aspect of human and natural existence,



As change is inevitable, as it is desirable



Yesterday as I stood at Times Square,



And later at Ground Zero and as I stood,



In awe and silence beneath the tallest black skyscraper,



I as Vision had a glowing vision,



Of an Obama sweeping across all barriers



To make the Global village smaller by holding the world economy



In his palm and see the world without any qualm.



It was then that I knew though I could not profess,



America’s time had come for a real time ahead



To monumentalise my minds eye of the,



Most inevitable of Creators’ orders that whatever it is



‘’L ET change be the cornerstone of all existence’’.



Rise thee Americans, above colour, caste, creed and religion,



Touch not values of personal consequence,



Rise above the level of snails’ speed,



To become a world an International leader indeed,



Come help the world out of an ailing depression,



Let economy flow out of recession and greet Obama,



With open arms, as he leads America beyond imagination,



To bring about a change, that the whole world wide needs



And stamp a mark of indelibility.



Let us join hands and ring in a New Year with Obama,



At the helm and let the International arena follow Obama.



God bless America and through the nation, Obama too,



Through him all the countries that make up a worldly village, a



Modern Times' indelible and deliberate creation.



‘’Hello Canada’s’’ Greetings for



‘’Hello America’’



Hope u all will like my  feelings for America, and through America, of the world.



</question>

<question from>



VISION
Member since: 05 January 2008
Total points: 12501 (Level 6)



</question from>



<question>



Are we all not glad that America has accepted CHANGE.? My love  4 change is boundless I am  a world's Anon, ?



incognito, citizen .



I like the best to win . I hate colour ,caste and creed and  consider Religion as personal. I  visit  churches, temples,monasteries, mosques and any such place ,to enjoy its silence and harmony and architecture.



Pease excuse me  for this Poetry, as I am no qualified poet, pseudo at best.THANK YOU.



LONG LIVE THE WORLD AND AMERICA



CHANGE ALONE IS PERMANENT



I recall Martin Luther King, some time long ago



He spoke ‘’I have a dream’’ so be it,



So must have Obama, the world needed the most indelible,



Also the only permanent aspect of human and natural existence,



As change is inevitable, as it is desirable



Yesterday as I stood at Times Square,



And later at Ground Zero and as I stood,



In awe and silence beneath the tallest black skyscraper,



I as Vision had a glowing vision,



Of an Obama sweeping across all barriers



To make the Global village smaller by holding the world economy



In his palm and see the world without any qualm.



It was then that I knew though I could not profess,



America’s time had come for a real time ahead



To monumentalise my minds eye of the,



Most inevitable of Creators’ orders that whatever it is



‘’L ET change be the cornerstone of all existence’’.



Rise thee Americans, above colour, caste, creed and religion,



Touch not values of personal consequence,



Rise above the level of snails’ speed,



To become a world an International leader indeed,



Come help the world out of an ailing depression,



Let economy flow out of recession and greet Obama,



With open arms, as he leads America beyond imagination,



To bring about a change, that the whole world wide needs



And stamp a mark of indelibility.



Let us join hands and ring in a New Year with Obama,



At the helm and let the International arena follow Obama.



God bless America and through the nation, Obama too,



Through him all the countries that make up a worldly village, a



Modern Times' indelible and deliberate creation.



‘’Hello Canada’s’’ Greetings for



‘’Hello America’’



Hope u all will like my  feelings for America, and through America, of the world.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



It's one thing to accept viable, valuable change.  It is altogether unacceptable to accept change in the name of change.  Currently, I am able to go a whole day without getting punched in the face.  However, to change my daily routine by adding a sucker punch to the eye socket every morning would be a negative change that is best done without.



</answer>

<question from>



=]
Member since: 29 February 2008
Total points: 94 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Can iambic pentameter very between the lines of a sonnet?



Or rather, am I allowed to start a line on the emphasized stress [the DUM] rather than on the emphasized one?



</question>



<answer from>



TD Euwaite™
Member since: 08 November 2007
Total points: 22097 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



No. In Poetic Engineering, the base form (Sonnet in this case) must be strictly adhered to. You can build a 14 line poem with 10 syllable lines, but it won't be a Sonnet.



</answer>



<answer from>



Elaine P
Member since: 04 May 2007
Total points: 33124 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



The meter is part of the Sonnet form. You must adhere to it or you'll have a poem that looks at first glance like a Sonnet, but will not be one.



</answer>

TD Euwaite™

<answer>



Ouilipo comes in many forms. Lady Professor showed them to us last year. There's one in my latest book, Pavlov's Cat. It is a style called N+7, where the SUBJECT NOUN in each line is replaced by the noun seven words ahead of it in the dictionary. FUN!

<question>



Yesterday was a bad day for me so I wrote down some thoughts I would like to share?



"How many times can a person be broken
before they shatter?
How many times can the heart be broken
before it no longer heals?
How many times can a person offer their hand in friendship
before that hand closes into a fist forever?
How many tears must I cry
before I learn?"



"Has the time come to no longer
love my fellow man, care for my fellow man,
call someone a friend?"



"Indeed that time has come
to harden my heart the way
others have.
To close my hand into a fist,
the way others have.
Gone is the heart that
loved so openly, without strings.
In its place is now a heart



with to many bandages to allow
new love in."



</question>

<question>



Have you found the one you know you will someday write?



This was going to be the one



the one that peeled your skin



back from your skull and made



you gush on the screen



blinded by stale blood



and exposed bone.



This was going to be



the human heart in your hand



the shattered glass eye



that saw every color of truth



I had to offer.



This was going to be the purebred



that raped the mutt



and turned the words on their edge.



I was hiding it but I have forgotten



how dark it was in there.



This was going to be



the one



but I can't find it any-
more.



</question>

<question from>



TD Euwaite™
Member since: 08 November 2007
Total points: 22003 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</question from>



<question>



If a writer has a limited vocabulary and catalog of expressions, will it be hard for him to write dialog?



</question>



<additional details>



Like when one guy is six avatars that all make the similar remarks from the same point of reference, always trying to validate a defensive posture.



</additional details>



<answer from>



Elaine P
Member since: 04 May 2007
Total points: 33011 (Level 7)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



It will be hard for him to write diverse dialog, since each dialog will sound similar or almost identical. Such writing will not engage the readers. The repetition will probably bore readers. Serious readers will eventually ignore such writing completely as a waste of time and energy.



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Did you rock the vote or vote the rock...hahahaha!



</asker's comment>



<answer from>



The Mighty Iano
Member since: 12 September 2008
Total points: 2051 (Level 3)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



This is indeed a strange and curious question. Not least of all because you have previously publicly admitted that you have various avatars, so surely you would already know the answer to your query. However, because of the peculiarities of language, there exists various catalogues of diverse expressions from which a large number of people can dip in and borrow, therefore giving a similarity of expression to their utterances, whether written or verbal. Educated, intelligent people tend to adhere to certain rules of spelling, punctuation and grammar which, to the casual and untrained eye, might suggest that their written epistles sprang from the same pen. Your puzzlement on this matter would be compounded if six different people were trying to sound like one person in order to confound you. Also, anybody with the slightest imagination would have not the faintest difficulty in varying his language in, let's say, 400 different identities, if it was his intention to project the illusion of numerous and separate personas for whatever purpose he wished.



Are you sure that you're not perhaps seeing what you want to see, in the same way that a person "smitten" by someone tends to see his beloved's face wherever he looks? I do so hope that my answer has been of help to you in getting to the root of your problem.



</answer>



<answer from>

Member since: 15 July 2007
Total points: 23965 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry

All 3 dressed, walked, talked, and acted differently.  Quite spooky.  And each personality was totally unaware of the other 2 for many years.  They were found and brought together with hypnosis.

<question>



Do most poets see the Ocean as male or female?



We have been discussing the poetic gender of the Ocean. Do you see it as personifying male or female aspects? Is the Ocean mother or lover? Life-giver or life-taker? Can you explain why you feel this way?



</question>



<additional details>



Intrus...you are speaking of linguistic gender. In poetry, you can't separate the ocean from its tides.

onyx-gol...

<answer>



I personally dont give it a gender per se, but I think depends on a lot of aspects.  What gender is the author, what are they writing about, as well as the general mood of the poem.  I am male, if I were writing about my wife coming back to me after a long trip and I am happy about this I would probably give the ocean a male gender, however if I was unhappy about this because I know she did me wrong while away i would give the ocean a female gender.  but that is just me.

<answer>



So much of the Ocean is associated with female. There are the sirens, the fact that the tides are controlled by the moon, also a poetic female entity. I'm not certain which place Ocean holds in my poetic mind. Most often when I am near her or thinking of her there is a peace within me. I don't feel this peace around male entities, so for me, in a poetic and literal sense, the Ocean is a female.



She is a giver of life, a thing of great beauty and awesome power. She also can take life and leave a land barren in her wake, also a power of women. Without women, there is no birth, therefore no life.



</answer>

<question>



For dearest Elaine...is this lightened up at all?



"Think Happy Thoughts"



Light flotation,
airy revelation,
singing,
scintillating observation.



World below,
peace of mind
held in hands
strong enough to love,
to give light to another,
saying
follow me beyond
transcend-dance.



Coins in wishing wells
becoming beating hearts,
the joys of each raindrop
painting a mosaic
of my smile.



Author's Note: Elaine, thank you.



</question>

<question>



Do you have a favorite bird?



I prefer the Blue Jay, a cunning bastard



that takes what he wants and leaves



the dirty worms dangling for his lessees.



Maybe his size is the reason I choke



when I try and vomit him up



during a nasty attack of solicitousness



and fear.



He waddles in excess and plummets



the depths of sky when tired.



When cold in winter



burning bushes



keep him warm.



</question>

<question>



Poem anyone? help! Please!!?



there's this guy at my job and he's always rapping and what not and he's hilarious. he asked me to write him a poem and i really wanted to but i suck. His name is Logan and I want to rap him something funny. I don't care what it is...i just need something! Please help! Thanks.



</question>



<answer from>



Kevin S
Member since: 23 June 2007
Total points: 16302 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Although Rapp is theoretically a poetic form, most of it is derivative and would otherwise be called "doggerel".  With this in mind, your "poem", if it is to be similar to Rapp, really doesn't need to be overly poetic, and by the nature of Rapp, can have many rhymed words or lines back to back without anyone caring about it being "rhymy".  That said, avoid the use of his name as a rhyming word.  It doesn't matter that you might be able to think about something that rhymes with Logan, just avoid it...you can say, "Logan's no fool, not anybody's tool, he likes to snap it, tapp it, while others try to rapp it..." etc.  Just enjoy yourself and have fun with it...it's not for a contest and he's probably only trying to have some fun...so have some fun with it and don't stress over how good the rhymes might be.  If you want to write a more conventional poem, then avoid rhymed couplets and still avoid using his name...it's too restrictive and puts too much stress on the name instead of his attributes.



...and keep writing :)



Source(s):



Editor, New Poets Press



</answer>



<asker's comment>



Thanks!



</asker's comment>

<answer from>



quaere verum
Member since: 06 October 2008
Total points: 554 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



I think that your first question is of no great consequence, but the second question you raise, while not poetic, is thought-provoking.  At this time, the answer regrettably seems to be (sadly) no; it cannot be found in the world at large, or in microcosm on this forum.  This is not a message of condemnation, but rather a matter of broadly held opinion. The problem, as I see it, is that entirely too many aspersions have been cast without thought, and no effort has consistently been made to correct this.  We have become a "nation" divided -- divided by aesthetic sensibilities and creative values -- and I'm not sure how we can turn back the clock.  It will require an uncommon amount of common sense, it will require perspective.  I hope your question, and my answer to it, will be a beginning, a beacon for the others to follow...



</answer>



<answer from>

Total points: 15917 (Level 6)

<question from>



DEATH ANGEL
Member since: 20 September 2007
Total points: 1717 (Level 3)



</question from>



<question>



This is a tribute to my late brother ELI...........Plz let me know if it's any good!!!?



ok so this is my very first poem...............i wrote it around three years ago................but my brother Eli died last year............i hav moved on but still cant stop thinkin' abt him...........so this one's for him.......



i love my brother, in my family
the way he held me, tight yet firmly
or the way he kissed my head



and wished a morning!



my day started when he sung me a song
"a day in the sun" by anneliese van der pol [ah-nah-li-zah]



after waking me up 5 in the morning
he asked me to be ready



and join him for joggin'



we took a shower, when we returned
it felt so great when calories burned
along the way, a few memories earned



when we used to get ready for office and school
wat if i get to spend the day with him?
wouldn't that be so much cool
i thought of several reasons



i m not feeling well, nor done my homework yet
mom used to know it all, for she ain't a fool



but when he heard, that i was feelin sick
he knew the reason behind my trick



he made an excuse
to get a leave from my school
he picked up his phone



and made a fake call
gettin' an appointment from the doc'
instead we hung out at a coffee shop
or along the park takin' a walk
checkin' out some hot chicks, while in the mall
or saw some flicks in a movie hall



entire day we would hang around
at the very end, in the park



we used to see that sun go down
then we took one last round



and then he took me on a long drive
we played our fav songs and felt that music's vibe



we went back home after long and tiring day
had our dinner and then some fun play
we had lot's of laugh, at the dinner table



then with some popcorn, it was time for cable



we then wishing a blissful night
went to our separate rooms
and turned down the lights
the night was so dark, yet so bright
for that was shining stars in the sky



he then entered my room, quite n slow
i opened up my eyes and said "hey, big bro"
he came near me and on my hair,



he put his hand to say a prayer
then he bent over and on my head
he laid a kiss and smiled and stared
about to leave,he stood up the bed



in a low and firm voice, he said
"you had a very wonderful day,
but dont you dare forget,
God's 'will' is to be obeyed,
to this cruel world,
someday if you might fall prey,
don't lose hopes, don't stay down,
for you must stand and say a prayer,
today i was here, but tommorow i might not be there"



that's my big brother, and i'm so proud to say
ELI STARLETT, one and the same...



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



that's so  sweet and heart felt but it needs some work, try re-reading it and thinking on it for a bit. i'm sorry for your loss

<question>



Read this poem... is it good?



Throat is tight
Hands are shaking
Breath comes quickly



Heart is quaking



Seeing his smile
Muddles my thoughts
Mind is blanked
Perception taught



My anger dissolves
When I look in his eyes
The power he holds
Will be my demise



I simply can't refuse him
With decent set precision
Those big blue eyes cloud up my mind
And nullify decision



If I were to place his hand
Where my heart should be
His eyes would widen with alarm
A ragged stutter of a beat



Trying to stay the rapid pace
Of my unruly straying heart
His smile melts my near success
And returns me to the start



Keeping feelings to myself
Is the smartest thing to do
If he knew the power he held
He could never let me go.



</question>

O Lord, our God, arise,

<answer>



What do I think of your poem? Or the sentiments expressed in it?



The poem; stanza two contradicts itself with the words 'voices cry'  and 'a wordless din of prideful joy
Poetic as Shakespeare'



Poetry is by definition words. A wordless din isn't. Shakespeare sure as hell wasn't a wordless din.



This come across as a simple bit of verse from a supporter of the winner, nothing profound.



The sentiments? ;- See how wonderful he seems in 4 years when the system has had a better chance to work on him. Then we may be able to judge him better - by results not promises.



Tony Blair seemed a wind of change and decency when he was elected here in Britain. He then presided over the administration that has destroyed a thousand years of British history, emasculated the Paliamentary process and obliterated countless personal freedoms in just ten years. We'll see how Barak fares against the machine. I wish him well, he'll need it.



</answer>

<question from>



traveling supervisor
Member since: 19 July 2008
Total points: 5913 (Level 5)



</question from>



<question>



Who better should I serve ? ?



thoughts, questions and poems



infinite complex contemplations,
mind bending, reaching, numbing.
are best achieved through more



than a few hearty drinks for some.
stubborn cranky fixation works too ?



not all life thoughts, questions, should be



glacial by, of, or in, their nature in my mind.
though some would devoutly, loudly insist,
wishing me to believe, embrace, their beliefs.
then chastising for not meeting expectations ?



some questions posed are, simply, simple,
quite mundane, low key, boring even.
their importance remaining a mystery,
their relevance known but to one.
who better should I serve ?



I believe I know what I was in my past,
possibly who I think I am, what I see.
nary a realistic hint of what I will be,



only what I dream to become tomorrow.
reality of your mind I should adopt ?



perhaps if the universe had listened, obeyed,
I could have charted my perfect life, of course.



I’d sail serenely along, without squalls,



upon self charted, placid blue, calm waters.
short sighted you, should be my guide, my pilot ?



the way to silence the mind is to kill it,



utterly and completely, by spiteful criticism.
thus, neither thoughts, nor life dreams,



nor simple questions will then remain.
when did I become enslaved to only your views ?



verses of mine shall, can, will, only provide,
images of my mind, my life, such as it is.
your hunger and thirst unsatisfied, you cry,



dreams, meanings, unrevealed by my meager life.
would you not benefit from opening your mind ?



I am no scholar, I cannot pretend
to be, what I am not, nor desire to be.
my livelihood is not dependent upon
words I write, just my sanity seems thus tied.
why is your lack of understanding so bitter ?



</question>



<answer from>



ma
Member since: 28 June 2008
Total points: 6451 (Level 5)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>

<question from>

Total points: 1953 (Level 3)



</question from>



<question>



Do you know this feeling?



I waited
Rain-soaked hair
With tear upon my
Hopeful cheek
Danced with time
As silent music
Slipped between
Hope and faith
Lay dwindling on the
Floor beneath my
Footsteps heard
i spun around
To see it wasn't you
Let down yet still
Clutched hope in
Hand made fist
And shadow grew
Upon the wall.



I waited



</question>

<question>



Will this poem still be here when I've returned from the conquest?



*****
SPRINGFIELD



Dust and ashes



fill the chamber,
clog the works,
foul the lock,



Film of oil



cleans the breech,
lock and barrel,
bail and block,



This one’s war
was years before us,
mounted fast,
unfought, unfired,



Reported silent
caked and crusty,
rusted anger,
blunderbuss.



*****



</question>



<additional details>



Blunderbusty?



</additional details>

<question>



Poem Project Help..????



I have a project that I need to complete for multimedia. I have to choose a poem and act it out and include pictures in a powerpoint. The only trouble is that I'm having trouble finding a poem that would be easy to act out. Can you guys help with some suggestions???



</question>



<answer from>



Ashley
Member since: 01 February 2007
Total points: 1180 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



I knelt to pray but not for long,
I had too much to do.
I had to hurry and get to work
For bills would soon be due.



So I knelt and said a hurried prayer,
And jumped up off my knees.
My Christian duty was now done
My soul could rest at ease...



All day long I had no time
To spread a word of cheer
No time to speak of Christ to friends,
They'd laugh at me I'd fear.



No time, no time, too much to do,
That was my constant cry,
No time to give to souls in need
But at last the time, the time to die.



I went before the Lord,
I came, I stood with downcast eyes.
For in his hands God held a book;
It was the book of life.



God looked into his book and said
'Your name I cannot find
I once was going to write it down...
But never found the time.'



Okay I don't know who the author was...and i think it would be simple to act out...but I don't know about ur religion so I'm not really sorry if it offends u but I do want you to understand I wasn't trying to offend you just trying to help you.



</answer>



<answer from>



Luna
Member since: 09 September 2007
Total points: 156 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



How long does it have to be? I perform poetry as a part of Speech and Debate, and our performances have to be ten minutes long...I usually do the Raven, which is a lovely performance piece.



Try "Goblin Market" by Christina Rosetti (although long, it has plenty of action), or, for something shorter and more whimsical, "Cloony the Clown" by Shel Silverstein.



</answer>

<question>



What's in your head these days ?



Once I knew a fella, of sorts,
an aggravating, bullheaded type.
Too full of himself, by half
all by himself, he remained.



Mastery of knowledge, emphatically,



he purported, with snobbery attitude.
Believed himself superior by far,
gratitude and applause he craved.



So often he tried to impress,
with diatribes proudly muttered.



Multi-syllabic nonsense, criticism,
flaming rants his sneering forte.



I asked him, respectfully, to please,



spare us spewings of pomposity.
Worthless, mirthless verbosity



when quiet is what will really do.



My request thrice, politely, quietly,



phrased, before being shouted.
You, sir, have your head, totally,



and completely up your ***.



</question>



<additional details>



not intended as a personal snip to anyone,,, I'd just had my fill of "full of themselves" folks at work yesterday and decided to vent a bit.



hip-lady,,, I could not agree more



</additional details>



<answer from>



Kevin S
Member since: 23 June 2007
Total points: 16313 (Level 6)

<question>



How many of these terms are new to you and me, especially that French one?



Basics of English Studies 4.2. Types of Poetry



When studying poetry, it is useful first of all to consider the theme and the overall development of the theme in the poem (see ch. 1.5.). Obviously, the sort of development that takes place depends to a considerable extent on the type of poem one is dealing with. It is useful to keep two general distinctions in mind (for more detailed definitions consult Abrams 1999 and Preminger et al 1993): lyric poetry and narrative poetry.



Key items:



lyric poetry
elegy
ode
sonnet
dramatic monologue
occasional poetry



epic
mock-epic
ballad
descriptive poetry
dramatic poetry
didactic poetry
prodesse et delectare



</question>

<question>



Help me finish this poem?!? please?!?



Delicate Memories



Each time i spy upon the sky
A single thought pops in my mind
It is always an image of you
My stunning best friend



Each time a tear rolls down my cheek
No matter how soft and meek
You seem to be the reason why
For I yearn for my best friend



As distant as we are
I will never overpass what we once had
I'll always remember you there for me
My helpful best friend



I miss you



I dont like the end I want to change it a little or add something to make it better, helpzz!!



</question>

<question from>



Wylie Nelson
Member since: 15 May 2008
Total points: 1116 (Level 3)



</question from>



<question>



Have you ever visited "Whiskey Row"?



Whiskey Row



In Old Town Prescott, Arizona
there is a legendary place
known simply as Whiskey Row
Late 1800's saloons stand
proudly together like friends
as they once stood before
their hardwood floors echo
sounds of worn cowboy boots
striding across to the bar
tin type photos line the walls
of days passed long ago
polished brass tube



aligns base of the bar



just a foot above the floor
where weary boots rested
after long, dusty ride
behind the bar sits a



mirrored lined wall
reflecting a century



of hard hitting drinking
by men whose lives



had hard hitting rules
the bar itself a massive plank



of rich red mahogany
hand carved work its ornament
beside sits a silenced upright
with inlays of multi-hued walnut



keys of ivory remain untouched
and are worn beyond repair



a testament that even



way back then, cowboys
demanded their air



to be music-filled.



</question>

<question from>



crooked
Member since: 01 July 2008
Total points: 152 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



What should my poem be called?



Please help me=] I am not asking for your opinions about my poem, just help me out with the title.



When I'm stuck in a hole all alone by myself
Everyone else runs away and tries to save themself
They hide from me and leave me to rot
Leave me to stare at my hands of what I don't got
Everyone's faces has a dark shine to them
Watching them act upon their feelings, something I condemn
It seems that My feet are on the wrong ground
While yours, there just bound
To the secrets you bear
Like I have secrets..like you care..
Nighttime, winter, times I wish you were here
I can't imagine just having you near
Here beside me grabbing me like you will lose me
But now I feel filthy, unworthy and empty



Who am I?
Where did I come from?
Why am I different from everyone else
Why am I rejecting myself
It's affecting everyone around me



She has no arms she's just a women with longer hair and a sader face
She stands stright up with her head up, and you can tell she found her own place
She's my imaginary friend, but with no real voice
She's more real then me I'm just a vision for someone else's confidence
Another page with see through words and blury pictures
Dirty lectures that teach me about ghosts I once knew then forgotten
Presure through my veins and life sends me an invitation to hell
Got some regrets I still hold dear to me
Got some cigarettes left over from when I wasn't me
So who am I if I aint her if I aint someone like you
Am I just pages of dead poetry from younger years?
Do I belong in this home with memories of tears?
Then hide all my fears away pretend they never excisted
Then wait for the bus even though I already missed it
Just keep walking with freezing hands and a cold mind
Reeching for a chance to speak trying to find a sign
To brace myself and wait will it ends...



Hanging from a cracked ceiling
Leaving myself screaming
Conceted



</question>

<question>



Have you even been in a "Ghost Town," like Jerome, AZ?



The Ghost Town
(Jerome, Arizona)



Mine stands dead
streets still lined
with whore houses
as dead as the mine



Tourists trample
the New Age stores
buying fake
souvenirs



Miner's ghost watches
with shake of head
his whore upon
his knee



Painted lady laughs
with glee and grinds
her ghastly form
into her man of the hour



Wind travels swiftly
off the cliff's edge
carrying echos of laughter
drenched in booze.



In famous coffee shop
father turns to child,
"we'll get your T-shirt soon
for show and tell in school



You can tell them all about
Jerome, a real live ghost town
and all the things you've seen."
And the wind swept off the cliff.



</question>

<question>



Is this poem good enough?



In my dark despair of torture and pain through my cold-blooded heart, i listen for the heartbeat of the demons. The distinction in their voices made me feel so frightened. . .confused in a way i couldn't explain.



This heart is going to fly away



disappear in the night of day



spread its wings and learn to fly



the questioning feed off whom comes by.



The light at the end of that pitch black tunnel



gradually becoming wider



opening my eyes to see



my one and only desire.



My love for him isn't nearly as true as the love i have for that sound



that sound, i thought, the screaching and screaming of death



knocking at my door.



i saw a flash of nothing pass by



and finally realized i wasn't alive



my last hours will remain right here



forever more, i shed a tear.



keep in mind, i'm only 12.
xoxo emma



&lt;33



</question>

<question>



Is your life filled with "Used to Be's"?



Used to Be's



Used to be's



are yesteryear's
past memories



though they be
used, worn and
tattered, they
remain treasured
in one's heart



unless one's day's
in constant thought
of remembering
used to be's
forever lost



forgetting that
tomorrow holds
the gift of promise
that one may find
new be's, not used.



</question>

<question from>



Angela D
Member since: 06 November 2008
Total points: 81 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Please tell me your opinion and thoughts of my brand new poem! 10 points to best answer.?



Hi! Please tell me what you think of my new poem.
I wrote it in a short amount of time and was just wondering what you thought.
Thanks!



Redeemed.



What was old, now is new;
A promise inaffected by what we do.



Mistakes have made us who we are;
Our evil is now locked behind prison bars.



The Battle with our downfalls now is won;
Light has washed away all we've done.



The Night is useless without it's stars;
Character pointless without it's scars.



One far greater than us has replaced our fear;
He prepares a place for us undimmed by tears.



To be free, we must believe;
A fufilled heart is what we recieve.



We've been set free from our prison;
All because our Savior is risen.



All our tears soothed, we live to see a brighter day;
All pain removed, we learn to let go of our old ways.



Everlasting light penetrates lingering dark;
not only in the skies, but also in our hearts.



My sins, lies, anger and hate forgiven;
to lead a better life, I now am driven.



</question>

<question from>



Robert Harrison
Member since: 20 November 2007
Total points: 2556 (Level 4)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</question from>



<question>



Is this rewrite any better?



I have tried to alter it to your liking, but if you feel there are more changes needed please feel free to make them. I have only included one ? as the rest are just repeating what Mrs Brown has said.



Robert



“Why, hello Mrs. Thomas and how are you today,
it’s been ages since I saw you, what is that you say?
Having tummy trouble are you, oh you poor dear,
told to take two bitter pills with a pint of Ansell’s beer.
Well that does seem strange I really must confess,
now you say you can’t fit into your band new dress.
I must say these doctors have some very funny ways,
if I were you my dear I would loosen off my stays.
You have done that have you, think you’re incontinent,
and are two weeks late, so now you must be pregnant.
Mrs. Thomas you cant be, for you must be sixty-five,
Still with ten kids at home and six having left the hive.
You need to watch what you eat, cut down in some ways,
eat more fruit why don’t you, and take off those silly stays.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



Hi Robert,



You need to focus on meter and stay true to it. From what you've written it seems as though you're going for iambic septameter couplets. If you want it to work, stay true to the form.



Consider the following re-write of your first couplet in true iambic septameter, and see how the rhythm flows:



Good Morning Mrs. Thompson, dear, and how are you today.
I haven't seen you in a year, so what have you to say?



Do you see what I mean? You need to keep the rhythm.



Hope this helps. Cheers, mate.



</answer>

<question from>



Missy Rogers

<question>



What do you think of this poem?



I feel so numb , so incredibly empty
Sorrow seeps through the cracks to find me.
I am not a brick wall , nor am I made of steel.
As a shooting star, I begin to fall
Plummeting into the depths of the earth
Shattering to pieces with all that I feel.
For there are not promises in the wind , they say.
The wind caressed my naked flesh
Then began to blow the other way.
I gaze up into the gloomy , gray , suffocating sky
As the rain commence we set ourselves free
And together we cry
I hold myself tight as I curl into a ball
I watch the day posses the night
And listen to the hushed voice of the blowing wind
Promise that it won't let me fall.
I turn my head away , for I can't bear to listen anymore.
I had listened to this familiar , faint voice on too many sleepless nights before.
For there are no promises in the wind
It will cast shivers up your spine , throw smiles to your heart,
And put fire to your soul
And with a sharp , gusty blow ,



The wind will carry it all away.



-Melissa B. Rogers  (17 years old)



</question>

<question>



A Poem called The Shrub - Can you let me know your thoughts?



From an infant seed, the shrub creeps quietly to the sunlight



Fragile coals ebb black and cold as they lose the last fight



Crystal raindrops crash with each dwindling, reckless dream



Surreal, warped worlds where almost nothing is as it seems



Thinning skin dissolves from scorching rays of dire despair



Broken hearts implode as the pain meets the cold cutting air



Tormented souls melt and unite with the poisoned icy rains



Dying beasts mercilessly devouring the rotting remains



Puddles of thick, rusty blood lay lifeless in craters of stone



Pulling desperately on branches that the sunlight had grown



Never quite dreaming enough to be a shadow-casting tree



Never quite fit to turn a lake into a wondrous, spirited sea



A hopeless shrub you shall stay with your limbs stripped away



The sun will turn to dust and your roots will turn to clay



Darkness will blanket what was left of your vacuous legacy



All that exists now is nothing, as far as these eyes can see.



</question>

<question>



A Poem Called Rainbow Slayer. Can you let me know your thoughts?



Tie me to your mind with strings made of dreams
Keep me sleeping



Wrap me up in manifestos and your regimes
Keep me weeping



Strand me on an island until I starve
Keep me dying



I'm a sculpture of a bird which you have carved
Stop me flying



Fill my eyes with your pictures laced with fear
Terrorise me



Play the songs only you want me to hear
Hypnotise me



Cut out my tongue and cast it upon the fire
Keep me silent



Attach the shackles of your hearts desire
Take my choices



Oh someone save me from this rainbow slayer.



</question>



<additional details>



It's not about a dream. It's about being oppressed by someone elses ideals i.e their dreams. "Terrorise me" is an integral part of this poem.



If you are misinterpreting that much, it's obviously not that good.



</additional details>

<answer>



I need to look at the Poem to give you proper answer...so where is the poem.I haven't seen it for quite a long time.



Well for the time being you can check the link below:
http://academic.brooklyn.cuny.edu/englis...
I think it may help you.

<answer from>



homersim...
Member since: 03 November 2008
Total points: 136 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



In "Ode on Melancholy" Keats accepts the truth he sees: joy and pain are inseparable and to experience joy fully we must experience sadness or melancholy fully. This ode expresses Keats's view wholeheartedly; it differs significantly from "Ode to a Nightingale" and "Ode on a Grecian Urn," in which the poet-dreamer attempts to escape from reality into the ideal and unchanging world of the nightingale and the urn. Keats valued intensity of emotion, intensity of thought, and intensity of experience; fulfillment comes from living and thinking passionately. Keats does not shrink from the implication that feeling intensely means that grief or depression may well cause anguish and torment



Source(s):



http://academic.brooklyn.cuny.edu/englis...



</answer>

<question from>

Member since: 04 November 2008

<question>



Conscience - A Poem I Just Wrote. Please Read On?



Conscience



Surrounded by these four walls,
Only solitude can she greet.
Hugging her knees,
Her eyes, blank with defeat.



She picks up a pen and began to write,
But stops at the words, "I am..."
Stared into space but continued,
"I am... but a sham."



"I wear a halo,
But I don't belong.
Stop saying I'm good,
This is wrong!"



"I've done nothing good,
Please open your eyes!
Can you see it?
This deceitful disguise?"



"I couldn't save her,
How can that be good?
It wasn't enough,
But I did everything I could!"



Tears of blood rolled down her cheeks,
As she continued to stare into space.
Reliving that very memory,
That she could never ever erase.



Writing, "I caused her death" over again,
These four walls, now her grave.
All because she was remorseful,
Of her daughter she couldn't save.



I'll leave you to decide on the story line, but what do you think of the poem? It just hit me really. So yeah.



xoxo,
Juvenal J.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>

<answer>



Boats Out In This Sea



Like two flowers in the sunshine
We watch each other grow
We sit and talk the time away
About things we'll never know



There's a gravitational pull
Like the earth and the moon
When I'm about to fall to pieces
You stand there with your glue



When I'm miles away from anywhere
You give me a taste of home
Within you is the kindest heart
That I have ever known



You would give the shoes off of both your feet
You'd give me your last pound (I'm from the UK)
You're a field of lush green grass
Upon this cold, cold ground



As the pages fill with fresh new words
And as the chapters end
Through our trials and tribulations
I hope you'll stay my friend



Because I never thought I'd find
Another boat out in this sea
I never thought I'd find
Someone as lost as me.



</answer>

<answer>



My Friend



You could stare at that scene for hours, but to you, I believe, would be as if a grave were across the threshold.



So dim, so serious, and laughter is quite a joy that gives pleasures to me, even if it's in vein across the threshold.



There's a small fluttering, so gentle, that it could rapture the very ground we stand on, the very moment we lost.



You wanted to run away from home, and it's so dim, so serious, that I'm not sure we'll find that moment we lost.



So I'm speaking aloud, being very idle about it, trying to give you hints that you may never notice my friend.
There's a distance I want to cross, that threshold is not longer permitting me to stay and watch sadly my friend.



</answer>

The end or the beginning?
by

Far across time and space,

<question>



How is my poem??????



“Awakening”



A tranquil sea of hope,



inundating waves of opportunity.



Blue washes upon infinite land;
isolation is carried into
depths of the sky.



Dawn envelops wonder,



and we gaze at



this endless realm with so blue,
smooth, real…clear.
(need one more line here-- any suggestions?)



To dusk, pinks and oranges



emerge from within this veil;
streaked sunset skies kindle
a twist in our lives:



color, flavor… an aberration.



Colors flourish, dance… disappear,
and night skies embrace sleeping towns.



Bright city lights twinkle, the spirit of the land
still present in the shadows.



No one sleeps alone.



When morning light shines,
how lucky to awaken anew



amongst this sea of never ending dreams,



streaks of color,
crystals of comfort.



Any suggestions for another line in that second stanza?
What do you think overall?
Any suggestions/things you would change?

What about this little freelance poem?



Time elapses upon my mind
As I search for things so hard to find
A distant star upon the sky
A silent call that leaves me bare
A warmth so bright it blurs my stare
A need so strong can't be dismissed
An endless kiss upon my lips
A feeling that I just can't forget
A sudden eclipse



Upon my soul
Searching , wanting , needing
No other than you , my eternal bliss.
Music breathing through the walls
Dancing with me in my domain
To see you , hold you once again
As lovers , equals and as friends



</question>

Elaina D

<question>



What do you think of my poem?



I want to know if my poem conveys a message and touches the heart.



I wrote this a little bit ago.
The topic is third world poverty.



WILL CHOOSE BEST ANSWER.



Saharma lives a life that grows harder and harder each day;



Why suffering affects an eight year old is a mystery on the African plains.



Orphaned with two younger brothers to be taking constant care of;



The only thing that gets them through is their unfailing love.



Forming clay bricks in dry desert heat;



she earns a cent a day trying to make ends meet.



Before attempting to sleep in a box made of cardboard;



the three little children pray for deliverance from the Lord.



Stealing bread scraps and dirty water from the market shop;



her brother grabs his exposed ribs and cries "Make the pain stop!"



Forced maturity on her part; nearly no one has her heart.



Their living conditions are horrendous, she hopes and prays for God to mend this.



The heat of the Sahara is comparable to the warmth of her heart;



The mighty power of the lion's run, is the strength of her faith when all is done.



Running quickly from the United Chinese Guard;



Lao says a quick prayer and grasps his sister's wrist hard.



He'll become a martyr for believing;



Every corner becomes deceiving.



Tucked deep away in his tattered coat's pocket;



he hides a small Gideon's bible and his mother's precious locket.



His tiny sister forms a silent cry:



"Lao, is this the day we're going to die?"



Lao tries to hide the tears and fears forming in his eyes;



"I don't know the answer to that, sweet Saku, but today we are truly alive.
They can take our food and shelter and we'll run if we must;
But never forget baby sister, who truly takes care of us.
Even now, though it's just you and me;
One day, like those in America, we too shall be free."



He holds her in his arms, singing the last lullaby she'll ever hear;



Though this life has passed, eternity is near.



Stories of those less fortunate than we;



As they suffer, at least we have the option to leave.



We're ungrateful for most everything;



Yet they take scraps as a gift from their king.



We complain as we look at our circumstances;



We don't realize that they're the ones who don't get second chances.



Our careers and material possessions rule who we are;



For those we disregard; love is what takes them far.



The kingdom of Heaven belongs to such as these;



Because they trust with their lives, the presence of God will never leave.



Why can't we have the faith of a child, the trust of an innocent, the love of a spirit mild?



Someday we'll find, we aren't of like mind.



America, wake up; Crisis may be, but as for me?



I trust in my God.



</question>

<answer>



I waited for endings to each of your sections; something to tie them all together that is not nebulous.  Also, when you post a poem with a space between the lines, then you have created, in essence, 40 stanzas; only in a manuscripts (mss) should your work be presented double spaced. It really throws the read off.



I don't think this falls into the category of poetry, but is more prosaic. I have found that my last few poems have this fault as well.  When something gets away from you it is hard to break it into multiple poems.



The lines ending:
The heat of the Sahara is comparable to the warmth of her heart;



The mighty power of the lion's run, is the strength of her faith when all is done.
are actually one poem. You can break the rest into about 2 more poems, and give the glory to God in each.t



</answer>

The gun lies on the floor

<question>



CALLING ALL POETS AND BLUE OYSTER CULT FANS!!!?



What the hell is ASTRONOMY about?  I'm a huge fan of the song especially the Metallica version. (apologies to the BOC fans but I love metal)  I'm been reading the lyrics over and over and I can not figure it out.  Wikipedia offered very little help, but atleast it was better than nothing.  So far I've got that the song is excerpts from a poem by Sandy Pearlman the origanl producer of BOC.  The poem was apparently intended to be a rock opera which spawned much of the "Imaginos" album.  There's some actual references to astronomy such as "the light that never warms" possibly refering to the moon, and "don't forget my dog, fixed and consequent" possibly refering to sirius.  I also read that the music video does not show the band whatsoever and only visualizes the story.  After a little 'youtub'ing I watched the music video and I am now more confused than ever, lol.  I want some of whatever Sandy Pearlman was on, when he produced that video.  Can anybody translate this song once and for all, or possibly find the actual poem in its entirety?



</question>



<answer from>



Grannyji...
Member since: 15 February 2008
Total points: 18139 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



The song's lyrics are selected verses from a poem by Sandy Pearlman, the band's producer and mastermind behind their image, called "The Soft Doctrines of Immaginos". In the poem, which was later released under the BÖC moniker as "Imaginos", aliens known as Les Invisibles guide an altered human named Imaginos, also called Desdinova, through history, playing key roles that eventually lead to the outbreak of World War I. In "Astronomy", the character of Imaginos comes to realize his heritage and his role as the altered human. References are made to celestial objects throughout the song-- "The light that never warms" being the moon, "The Queenly flux" the constellation Cassiopeia, "My dog, fixed and consequent" being Sirius, the dog star. The "Four Winds Bar" may be a reference to the Tropic of Cancer. All in all, it has Imaginos explaining his position as part of Les Invisibles.



I expect you've read this already, I copied it from Wikepedia - still it might jolt some-one else's memory



</answer>
