<answer>



I did not buy their first album. I heard some of it on the radio and then rushed out and got "Tyranny and Mutation."



It was all very average. They had some good tunes, but I consider them a One-Hit-Wonder with "Don't Fear the Reaper" as their seminal piece of music.



I missed the later stuff. By then, I had discovered classical music and never went back to Acid Rock. Even today, when I hear most American heavy metal from my school days, I say to myself, "What was I thinking?"



Today, much of the best music from the Hard Rock Gods (Led Zeppelin) fails the test of time, with the best pieces featuring Mr. Plant's falsetto and Mr. Page's mandolin.

<question>



What is your opinion of this edited descriptive poem?



Sunrise
by Elaine Polin



Dawn breaks
over still waters
tiny ripples
touch the sand
gulls soar
crying morning greetings.



The golden orb
springs from the sea
rises slowly
brightening the sky
I squint
to see its glory.



Light envelopes
my dark room
spreading slowly
over my dreams
I rejoice
in morning light.



</question>

<category>

<question from>



TD Euwaite™
Member since: 08 November 2007
Total points: 22080 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</question from>



<question>



More from BOES: has your reading workload gone up considerably?



4.2.1. Lyric Poetry



A lyric poem is a comparatively short, non-narrative poem in which a single speaker presents a state of mind or an emotional state. Lyric poetry retains some of the elements of song which is said to be its origin: For Greek writers the lyric was a song accompanied by the lyre.



Subcategories of the lyric are, for example elegy, ode, sonnet and dramatic monologue and most occasional poetry:



In modern usage, elegy is a formal lament for the death of a particular person (for example Tennyson’s “In Memoriam A.H.H.”). More broadly defined, the term elegy is also used for solemn meditations often on the question of death, such as Gray’s “Elegy Written in a Country Churchyard.



An ode is a long lyric poem with a serious subject written in an elevated style. Famous examples are Wordsworth’s “Hymn to Duty” and Keats’ “Ode to a Grecian Urn.”



The sonnet was originally a love poem which dealt with the lover’s sufferings and hopes. It originated in Italy and became popular in England in the Renaissance, when Thomas Wyatt and the Earl of Surrey translated and imitated sonnets written by Petrarch (Petrarchan Sonnet). From the seventeen century onwards the sonnet was also used for other topics than love, for instance for religious experience (by Donne and Milton), reflections on art ( by Keats or Shelley) or even the war experience (by Brooke or Owen). The sonnet uses a single stanza of (usually) fourteen lines and an intricate rhyme pattern (see stanza forms ch. 4.5.). Many poets wrote a series of sonnets linked by the same theme, so-called sonnet cycles (for instance Petrarch, Spencer, Shakespeare, Drayton, Barret-Browning, Meredith) which depict the various stages of a love relationship.



In a dramatic monologue a speaker, who is explicitly someone other than the author, makes a speech to a silent auditor in a specific situation and at a critical moment. Without intending to do so, the speaker reveals aspects of his temperament and character. In Browning’s “My Last Duchess” for instance, the Duke shows the picture of his last wife to the emissary from his prospective new wife and reveals his excessive pride in his position and his jealous temperament.



Occasional poetry is written for a specific occasion: a wedding (then it is called an epitalamion, for instance Spencer’s “Epithalamion”), the return of king from exile (for example Milton’s “Lycidas”), etc.



</question>



<additional details>

OK, maybe three or four, tops.

Your gaze did not rest on me

<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



I think if you're deciding between poem's meaning and rhyme the meaning is much more important, and also the flow of the poem is more important than the rhyme,



rhyme is like an added bonus it can be poetry without it, So I would say at some parts where you felt you had to use this word because it was the only one that rhymed go back and switch it with what you wanted there and it might look more natural



</answer>

night comes quickly that is alll i pray

<question>



What is your opinion of this edited descriptive poem?



Sunrise
by Elaine Polin



Dawn breaks
over still waters
tiny ripples
touch the sand
gulls soar
crying morning greetings.



The golden orb
springs from the sea
rises slowly
brightening the sky
I squint
to see its glory.



Light envelopes
my dark room
spreading slowly
over my dreams
I rejoice
in morning light.



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



At first I was taken aback by 'springs from the horizon, then rises slowly'...but, then, that's exactly what it does! No conflict with springs and slowly...
Good one...this reader saw what you described...good one!



</answer>

26 Words
by Elaine Polin



When the clusters
whispers
black I
despair in
that
currents
the words

welcome
to majestic
once I’ve
why the
I’ve, I’ll

the
allowing.

<question>



For What Loves Worth - Judge my Poem :)?



For what loves worth, I would do anything
For what loves worth I would give everything
A million gold pieces could not make
My Eternal sense of love become fake
From the many likes and loves I have had
Thou all not great, I’ll nor forget or be sad
Because what loves is and what it means most
Is it’s just as simple as Jam on Toast.
The Lady being the red loving heart
The man being the heart-warming old tart/fart
Thou love may not work, or perhaps it’ll thrive
If not, for what loves worth you will survive
Nothing in the world can replace love’s worth
This is shown through a little child’s birth
Nothing else but love forms this unique life
If at first it won’t work, don’t be in strife
Just take a chance, fall in love, have a laugh
Be ready for the day, you find your path



My real first try at being a poet :)



Thanks Constructive Critism appreciated
10 Sylables Per line I think

<question from>



Wylie Nelson
Member since: 15 May 2008
Total points: 1116 (Level 3)



</question from>



<question>



Have you ever visited "Whiskey Row"?



Whiskey Row



In Old Town Prescott, Arizona
there is a legendary place
known simply as Whiskey Row
Late 1800's saloons stand
proudly together like friends
as they once stood before
their hardwood floors echo
sounds of worn cowboy boots
striding across to the bar
tin type photos line the walls
of days passed long ago
polished brass tube



aligns base of the bar



just a foot above the floor
where weary boots rested
after long, dusty ride
behind the bar sits a



mirrored lined wall
reflecting a century



of hard hitting drinking
by men whose lives



had hard hitting rules
the bar itself a massive plank



of rich red mahogany
hand carved work its ornament
beside sits a silenced upright
with inlays of multi-hued walnut



keys of ivory remain untouched
and are worn beyond repair



a testament that even



way back then, cowboys
demanded their air



to be music-filled.



</question>

<question>



New poem, that which i wrote...the sun watches...what do you think?



the sun shines in the sky
looking down upon the earth
watching the people
who inhabit this land
the people who fight
the wars that they start
the death that they cause



how can the sun bear to watch us kill each other?
how can the sun bear to watch the misery?
how can the sun bear to watch the disease?
the plague which has spread across the earth?



The moon comes,



here to relieve the sun,
to give old yellow a rest
the moon watches too,
with a half eye or a full,
the moon sees, the stars see



Will the people of the earth
ever lay to rest
all the conflicts,
all the fighting,



all the bloodshed,
the unkindness committed upon one another?



The day the sun watches,
the night the moon comes,
and the stars shine,
they are bright, brighter than before
bright the time the people stop,
bright with joy,
bright with peace.



i made that up as i went along...
unedited, i just felt like writing another poem...
i think i have poem fever =)
anyway, constructive criticism would be appreciated =D

<question>



PLZ HELP!! do u like this poem? :D plz read :)?



Words have meaning



She wakes up in the morning to her parent’s hurtful words
They call her a disappointment, a burden in their lives



She tries to hide her tears and keep her head held up high
They swear and hit her for not getting straight A’s
She walks to school staring at the morning sun’s rays
Walking to school, dreading the day.



She walks through the gates to hear laughter and mocking
They won’t stop making fun of her black clothes and makeup



She pulls her sleeves right past her fingers
They can tell she’s hiding something under them
She cries as they poke fun at her.
She was told she was ugly



and the world would be a better place without her.



She walks to her locker sad and confused
They tip her and shove her, throw her books
She opens her locker to find a note that says
They might not love you but I do,



I would take the bullet for you
Life is nothing without you.



She walks home from school feeling lonely and depressed
The horrible things people said that day running through her head
She had heard it enough from them and her parents so she starts to believe it
Her mother grabs her by the hair and shoves her into her room
She takes out the note and reads it over
She rips it and throws it into the bin



Early the next day her father and mother walked into her room
Their faces had changed when they saw her limp body hanging from the fan
A note by her bed saying sorry I’m not perfect,
Only in one persons eyes



A man is sad, depressed destroyed
His heart was ripped out about the news
He couldn’t understand why people who handed her the rope
Were laughing and talking as if nothing happened



Three days past a young boy is found dead
A bullet shot into his head
There was note by his bed
It said.
I told you I would take the bullet for you
Life is nothing without you.



</question>

<question>



My brand new poem! Opinons and thoughts please?



Hi! Please tell me what you think. =] 10 points to best answer.



Redeemed.



What was old, now is new;
A promise inaffected by what we do.



Mistakes have made us who we are;
Our evil is now locked behind prison bars.



The Battle with our downfalls now is won;
Light has washed away all we've done.



The Night is useless without it's stars;
Character pointless without it's scars.



One far greater than us has replaced our fear;
He prepares a place for us undimmed by tears.



To be free, we must believe;
A fufilled heart is what we recieve.



We've been set free from our prison;
All because our Savior is risen.



All our tears soothed, we live to see a brighter day;
All pain removed, we learn to let go of our old ways.



Everlasting light penetrates lingering dark;
not only in the skies, but also in our hearts.



My sins, lies, anger and hate forgiven;
to lead a better life, I now am driven.



</question>

emmamac

<answer>



A catalogue of missed targets. 
Unintentionally funny, because of its ridiculous vocabulary and absurd images: 
"spawned by" an "ego"?
"mountainesque persona"?
"tongue in burnt discussion"?
"heart felt phalanges"?
"throngs of passion"?
Get hold of a good dictionary and/or thesaurus, and think about what you really want to say here, because as it stands it's an epileptic rhino.



</answer>

<question>



Does anyone know a good peom for my mum's funeral?



Hi! I'm looking for a poem for my mum's funeral, she was a keen gardener. Does anyone have any ideas?



</question>



<answer from>



Smurf
Member since: 12 April 2007
Total points: 1513 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



I'm afraid It's got nothing to do with gardening, but this is one of the most beautiful poems I've ever heard. It doesn't have a by-line, but it was written and circulated after the 9-11 attacks.

If I knew it would be the last time
That I'd see you fall asleep,
I would tuck you in more tightly
and pray the Lord, your soul to keep.

If I knew it would be the last time
that I see you walk out the door,
I would give you a hug and kiss
and call you back for one more.

If I knew it would be the last time
I'd hear your voice lifted up in praise,
I would video tape each action and word,
so I could play them back day after day.

If I knew it would be the last time,
I could spare an extra minute
to stop and say "I love you,"
instead of assuming you would KNOW I do.

If I knew it would be the last time
I would be there to share your day,
Well I'm sure you'll have so many more,
so I can let just this one slip away.

For surely there's always tomorrow
to make up for an oversight,
and we always get a second chance
to make everything just right.

There will always be another day
to say "I love you,"
And certainly there's another chance
to say our "Anything I can do?"

But just in case I might be wrong,
and today is all I get,
I'd like to say how much I love you
and I hope we never forget.

Tomorrow is not promised to anyone,
young or old alike,
And today may be the last chance
you get to hold your loved one tight.

So if you're waiting for tomorrow,
why not do it today?
For if tomorrow never comes,
you'll surely regret the day,

That you didn't take that extra time
for a smile, a hug, or a kiss
and you were too busy to grant someone,
what turned out to be their one last wish.

So hold your loved ones close today,
and whisper in their ear,
Tell them how much you love them
and that you'll always hold them dear

Take time to say "I'm sorry,"
"Please forgive me," "Thank you," or "It's okay."
And if tomorrow never comes,
you'll have no regrets about today.

xx



</answer>



<answer from>

Total points: 3227 (Level 4)

<answer>



Do not stand at my grave and weep

Do not stand at my grave and weep;
I am not there. I do not sleep.
I am a thousand winds that blow.
I am the diamond glints on snow.
I am the sunlight on ripened grain.
I am the gentle autumn rain.
When you awaken in the morning's hush
I am the swift uplifting rush
Of quiet birds in circled flight.
I am the soft stars that shine at night.
Do not stand at my grave and cry;
I am not there. I did not die.



</answer>

<answer>



Remember
by Christina Rosetti



Remember me when I am gone away, 
Gone far away into the silent land; 
When you can no more hold me by the hand, 
Nor I half turn to go yet turning stay. 
Remember me when no more day by day 
You tell me of our future that you plann'd: 
Only remember me; you understand 
It will be late to counsel then or pray. 
Yet if you should forget me for a while 
And afterwards remember, do not grieve: 
For if the darkness and corruption leave 
A vestige of the thoughts that once I had, 
Better by far you should forget and smile 
Than that you should remember and be sad.

or



In Memory Of My Mother
by Patrick Kavanagh

I do not think of you lying in the wet clay
Of a Monaghan graveyard; I see
You walking down a lane among the poplars
On your way to the station, or happily

Going to second Mass on a summer Sunday-
You meet me and you say:
'Don't forget to see about the cattle-'
Among your earthiest words the angels stray.

And I think of you walking along a headland
Of green oats in June,
So full of repose, so rich with life-
And I see us meeting at the end of a town

On a fair day by accident, after
The bargains are all made and we can walk
Together through the shops and stalls and markets
Free in the oriental streets of thought.

O you are not lying in the wet clay,
For it is harvest evening now and we
Are piling up the ricks against the moonlight
And you smile up at us - eternally.



</answer>

<question>



How To Identify Symbolism In Poetry...



How does the average person identify the symbolism in poetry? I need to write a poem for an assignment and must include a creative symbol and I'm looking to find examples because I dont know exactly what symbolism is.



</question>



<answer from>



Todd
Member since: 22 May 2006
Total points: 17128 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



Symbols are everywhere in life. A symbol is one thing used to represent another.

They are asking for a creative symbol so you'll have to come up with something that isn't overused. Here are a few common one's for you:

Dove symbolizes peace.

Scales symbolize justice.

The blindfold on the justice statue symbolizes impartiallity.

It is using an image to mean something more. To convey an additional nuance.

I hope that helps.



</answer>



<answer from>



Grannyji...
Member since: 15 February 2008
Total points: 13959 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



A symbol is something which typifies a myriad things, encapsulates them, I suppose you could say.....so something which (to me) represents/symbolises Canada is a maple leaf (check out Wikipedia if you want more on this).
An eagle is symbolic of America....in writing, I remember from college, symbolism can be difficult to detect.....but, say in D H Lawrence's novels Horses symbolise - sex (or so they say).
The sea can be symbolic of - the earth's life blood, or a means of washing away sin, or people's moods (anger, calm, peaceful....actually that might be the one to use for your poem)



Source(s):



Edit - My anger rages like the sea



I want to toss rocks with equal ease



And pound them into grains of sand



To wash ashore in foreign lands



(then change to another mood.... )



</answer>

<question>



Poetry publishers need a list of?



I am typing my poems out onto paper and I require the addresses of publishers.Magazines or what ever.Money would be nice too....



</question>



<answer from>



Leah M
Member since: 13 December 2006
Total points: 2192 (Level 3)



</answer from>



<answer>



You need to get hold of the Artists and Writers Yearbook, it lists every publisher in the UK and some in America as well.  It tells you what each publisher specialises in and I think it lists some magazines that publish stuff as well.  You'll be sure to find lots of people in there to reject your work (I'm not bitter, honestly!!)



</answer>



<answer from>



Kevin S
Member since: 23 June 2007
Total points: 14692 (Level 6)



Contributing In:



Poetry



</answer from>



<answer>



The single best source for poetry publishers is "Poets Market".  It covers publishers in the U.S. and comes out every year.  In it you'll find lists of publishers, what kind of poetry they want, what, if any compensation you'll receive if they choose to publish your poem, how to submit your poems, where to submit them, how to write letters of introduction, etc.  Basically, everything you need to know about how to submit poetry, where to submit it and whether or not your poetry is even the right "style", "form" or "type" for the publisher.  If your local library doesn't have a copy, your local bookstore will, or can certainly order it for you within a few days.



Source(s):



Editor, New Poets Press



</answer>

<question>



Come into the Garden Maud - Part II.  What do you think?



What he said next
Come into the Garden Maud
(Alfred, Lord Tennyson)
.....I wait for it to be deleted by one of the beings who dwell in the ether

I'm waiting patiently for thee
See me here, neath the apple bough
Shaded by this ancient tree.
Have I not waited long enow?
Come, darling, here and sit with me
You cannot refuse me now.

See the dainty daisies yawning
Faces kissed by the rising sun.
Bathed in sweet dew of the morning
Relishing the prize that they've won.
You are like these daisies dawning
Fresh, unsullied....my sweet one.

enow - old English for 'enough' see quote below to prove I'm not fibbing

"If we are mark'd to die, we are enow
To do our country loss; and if to live,
The fewer men the greater share of honour."
William Shakespeare (1564-1616); King Henry V



</question>

<question>



Do you like my poem?



There is no star, nor all in union –
Can match the radiance of you.
The universe is a dusty shroud
It’s only you who shines through.

Now let all of creation be eclipsed - 
Every celestial body snuffed out.
I want for no lark or nightingale
Sweeter are you even if you shout.

Burn all the worlds’ texts of faith 
Gauged to you they are not divine.
I could listen to your words all day
Wisdom from your lips –
Sublime…



</question>

<answer>



I really enjoyed it.  Why not get it published?  I've loved writing since I was at primary school some 40 years ago but had never had anything published.  I work from home now as a typist and decided, while I was waiting for some work to come in, that I'd dig out some of my old work.  Found a website www.triond.com which publishes all sorts of work and you get paid per view; not huge amounts initially but, if you're like me, you'll become completely possessed!!  Every spare minute at the moment is spent typing up new articles (my speciality) and I'm now dragging out a couple of children's short stories I did over 10 years ago.  Triond is free to use too!  If you go to my profile you can have a look at what I've written over the last month.  Good luck!



Source(s):



www.triond.com

<question>



A new poem; could you please comment



" My Last Cigarette"



I cough, but it makes no difference
the chest draws tighter each day
hard to keep on breathing
the stress is her to stay

A lack of stamina prevents me
it takes me to a place of solitude
away from the things I should have done, not said
I wish there was another way

A daily cycle of breathlessness
unable to be the one
that plays with their children and teaches them
all the things I once found fun

A chosen monotony 
I can’t escape
I am in need of a fix right now 
my mind is thin, my will caves in
temptation to much to bear

When will it come
this resolution
I am eager to place my bets
that once and for all
this time I won’t stall
and have my last cigarette



(Copyright © Geoffrey Brett - 02/08/2008)



</question>

<answer>



The stress is here to stay (I know you know that....but, I can't help myself)

As a series of verses this is fine....but as a poem, it could do with being tidied up 
The first verse introduces a rhyme scheme, the second verse ignores it (and third line is too long in second verse, ditto third verse)....that kind of thing.
Check it over - it is worth doing some revision to, since it has a lot to say (and mostly says it well)
temptation too much to bear (sorry!)
Last verse nicely put...it sounds emphatic, but we are left thinking'Oh, yes - heard that one before'
I gave up cold turkey 20 years ago...it can be done.



</answer>

<question>



Review this please , cant wait to hear comments



Leaving

By Ru Hewage- Copyrights@ruhewage

Turned me out into the red
The price of love I guess
On a burner in the corner
It goes on 
Don’t remember where it was
That I said my ABC’s

Back then it 
It was flowers all the days
Lucky now if you don’t
Decide to play 
Paint my face

Trying hard 
To gather bits of me
Take the boldness
Walk out the door
Never look back



Why do I stay
I really don’t know 
Twisted the core
Now there’s nothing



I try to sit 
Watch another day
Something tells me
Troubles on its way

Wear my brave hat
Pack my bags
Hear a knock 
Hide the bags
Thank god it’s
Just the mailman

Not willing to 
End up a statistic
I will ease myself
Off the burner
Leave a note
Maybe not



Stop in the hall
Look to the wall
You smiley eyes 
Follow me through
Reach the door way
Then I turn back 
Grab a smiley face
March myself to the door
Leaving you behind



</question>

<question>



Pls rate this poem.....????????



Exquisitely 
© 2008 LMN

We are one intertwining 
In exquisite oneness
Eyes turn when we step in bliss
Our handsome collection of fruitful
Bliss
Heaven is here, I’m assured
It is the look you give
So intense
Causing a burning desire for your hungry hands
The chivalry of your language
So enticing
Addictive
I will remember the silk of our
Pleasure 
The calming eyes of the gentle cloud
Shining over our glowing faces
Tomorrow is but a pleasure 
Of reliving
Re-touching
Of fine wines
Lovely dinners
Red roses and chocolates
We can live here
You and I and just beam
Until tomorrow 
When we’ll do it all again



</question>

<question from>



Llortama...
Member since: 09 June 2008
Total points: 618 (Level 2)



</question from>



<question>



What do you think of the latest piece of troll poetry? Could it be expanded into an elegy? ?



Along the city streets, and by
The avenues, the people fly;
All rushing, going God-knows-where,
Round Marble Arch, Trafalgar Square,
Yet in the midst of all this haste,
All those with ample time to waste,
Can find among the hustling host
A place invisible to most,
The house of all the living souls
‘Tis called The Palace of the Trolls.

Here lingering by the gate, I spied
The Princess of the Trolls inside.
She beckoned me and though I would
Have tarried outside, found I could
Not e’re resist the maiden’s call
To enter in her sacred hall.

She was a lass, quite simply dressed,
She was a blonde (you might have guessed).
I asked “What is it with the trolls
What do you do, what are your roles?
“Trolls are the very heart of wit,
Although their answers sound like ****.
I ask the dumbest questions yet
And ever stupid answers get
From punters greener than the grass
I make the suckers kiss my ***.

This is the kind of stuff I mean,
You’ll see I try to keep it clean
‘What lies due North above North Pole?
Next president to be Bob Dole?
And have you any gambling tips?
And why do oranges have pips?
And rat-a-tat ‘bout this and that
And why are pizzas always flat?

And still they answer every day
For all the suckers come my way.
So why do Yahoo Answers moan
And say the fault’s with us alone?
Just put the blame on simple souls
And never criticise the trolls.



</question>

<question>



What do you think this poem is about?



10 points for the best answer.

Its scorching tongues seek to lick and swallow,
Beckoning to join the idiot dance;
Even the shadows are seduced to follow
The lure of the flames, the dangerous trance.

Come closer, closer, to the fire that wakes
And coaxes from us elemental power:
Spitting their hot venom, these darting snakes,
Mad with their desire to breed and devour.

Between fiery promise and spiteful heat,
There rides the balance in the swaying flames:
Life's focus is that bright and friendly beat,
The same that runs through Satan's ravenous games.

The altar, warm with fire-seeds newly sown,
Cradles the force that Hell will make its own.



</question>

<answer>



My take on it is that the poem speaks of our carnal desires and how it eventually leads to our downfalls. Fire, shadows, snakes and Satan all represent danger in a tempting form while many of the other words are linked to our bodily appetites (lick, swallow, seduce, lure, breed, devour etc). The final two verses seem to revolve around the submission to the sin and the sinner's eventual damnation.

Awesome poem though, could you tell me who's it by and what its called?

<question>



Poem: "Technology". Comments?



My great-grandad George was a merry old soul
Though some would say his smile was smug.
He mocked and he scoffed at the family's concerns
When he caught the technology bug.

"Look! Horseless carriages and moving pictures too,
And machines that can fly through the air!
These gigantic steamers and new express trains
That take you in a blink here to there!"

As a man then must
He proved his deep trust
And his faith in Science's news
By going off, if you please,
To sail the high seas
And cross over to the States on a cruise.

He laughed: "Babies, don't cry!
And technology's why:
I'll tell you in truth how I am.
I'll wire you each day 
Whilst I am away
By state of the art telegram!"

And as he sailed away
One sharp springtime day
We waved tearful goodbyes on the quay,
And true to his word
Every day we heard:
"I'm fine - ship's fine too - you see?"

A ragged photograph proves the truth of this yarn:
My great grandpa grinning large as life in the stern.
And there on the lifebelt (still no need to panic)
Is the name of the ship: the SS Titanic.



</question>



<additional details>



Vari-able:
You have my sympathy.
I hope you recover from your sense of humour by-pass soon.



Many thanks, Iano, for taking the time to peruse, and suggest improvements.
I'll take most on board (so to speak), apart from the last verse, which I think has to end with "Titanic" - punch line, and all that.



</additional details>



<answer from>



Iano
Member since: 14 July 2008
Total points: 131 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Now this is better and shows imagination. Few rough lines though. How about....



(HAVE REVISED IT AGAIN.)



My great-grandpa Cole was a daring young soul,
self-assured without being smug.
He scoffed at his wife's and his children's concerns
when he caught the 'technology bug'.

"Look! Trams in a groove and pictures that move,
and machines that can fly through the air.
These gigantic steamers and new express trains
that can move in a blink here to there."

So as brave men must, he did prove his deep trust
and his faith in Science's views,
by going, if you please, to traverse the high seas
and sail to the states on a cruise.

He said "Do not cry! And technology's why -
I'll keep you informed on the way.
I'll wire you a note for each day I'm afloat
by telegraphed communique!"

And, as he sailed out, with a fond farewell shout
they waved their goodbyes on the quay.
And, true to his word, each new day they heard: 
"Ship's fine, so don't worry 'bout me!"

In case you should fail to believe in this tale,
a torn photograph proves its truth,
of great-grandpa smiling, all hearty and hale
and still in the prime of his youth.

He stands and he waves, he's a man of the age,
relaxed, with no sign of panic...
the name on a lifebelt from history's page
declares - the SS TITANIC!

Strictly speaking, it would be 'telegraph' (I think), not 'telegram'.

A torn photograph proves the truth of this tale -
my great-grandpa smiling, so hearty and hale,
next to a lifebelt, with no cause to panic,
showing the ship's name - the SS TITANIC!

Right! That's enough from me - get to work and finish it off.

'So wise and so sage, he's a man of the age,' perhaps?



Source(s):



Innate ability.



</answer>

<question>



Is this poem any good?



Just Friends???



We hang out.
We have a laugh.
But now I can't stop thinking about what we could have.
He thinks where just friends.
But I want more.
I feel we will fall out.
If he found out.
My heart flutters when he is near.
When i look at his gorgeous brown eyes.
I feel like i'm melting inside.
But I know deep down it won't work out.
I'll friendship will end if I tell him the truth.
So I must keep quiet.
Hide my feelings.
It will be hard.
But I will try,
I'll let my feelings lie. 
Until the right time floats by.



</question>

<answer>



I got a poem for my birthday,



He seemed to write so nice,

the words seemed genuine to me,



I read that poem thrice,

and skipped for joy,



he loved me



but later occured to me,

if i erased my name and "birthday"



could be for some one else

did he?

write this to someone else and then

give this poem to me?

For in the poem were words that held no



meaning between us two,

it seemed written for another lover,

and how they met and found



each other, the prose was



foreign to our relation

but to some other women,

oh the deflation! Of a birthday poem

not written
just for me.



It can rhyme, but it should have meaning, personal experience, emotion is nice, but not needed, rhyming? not needed. 
Poety is art, in prose



</answer>



<answer from>



garden girl
Member since: 11 August 2008
Total points: 335 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



I don't believe just saying a group of words is a poem makes it a poem. For a group of words, rhyming or not, to be a poem it should invoke emotion, give a visual, make a statement, tell a story ect. Many people write poems to express emotion rather than invoke it. They tell you how they feel instead of using the words to make you feel it, which I believe is what a good poem does.



</answer>

morporc

<answer>



In most types of language what is being said matters, but how it is being said is not very important.

'Pass me the biscuits' and 'Pass those biscuits to me' mean the same thing, and ordinarily one would be as good as the other.

But sometimes the exact words that are used when a thing is said can be important. (Sometimes even more important than the thing said).

When the words begin to matter as much as (or more than) the message, you have poetry.



'My father began to read us out of 'Narnia'. We watched the wardrobe open on a snowstorm.'



</answer>

<answer from>



Fortunat...
Member since: 18 July 2008
Total points: 349 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



The only real definition of poetry is that it's language in condensed form.



The primary element of poetry is not meaning, but form. "All my life," said W. H. Auden, "I have been more interested in technique than anything else". T. S. Eliot wrote that "the conscious problems with which one is concerned in the actual writing are more those of a quasi-musical nature, in the arrangement of metric and pattern, than of a conscious exposition of ideas."

That's why poetry that doesn't rhyme is still poetry - it has a pattern, it has a structure. It's an arrangement.



The confusion surrounding poetry, however, is due to the kind called "free-verse" - poetry which has no fixed pattern or structure. This is a new kind of poetry, and the majority of it is total rubbish. It basically breaks ALL the rules. You have to be a real master to make anything readable out of it. And, unfortunately, its the kind that most people try to write.



If poetry is like painting, free verse is like using pencils, pens, acrylics, oils, watercolours, and everything else you can get your hands on, all at once. You'd have to REALLY know what you're doing to produce anything decent. Otherwise you're just a kid playing with an art set.



Hope this ramble helps. If you want to learn more about poetry, but want to avoid the mass of boring and overly-technical books on the subject, look for Stephen Fry's 'The Ode Less Travelled'. It's brilliant, funny, and easy to read. It's much better than the majority of books suggested on my course, and it teaches much more!



</answer>

<answer>



By asking others to finish your poem for you, you are compromising its artistic integrity. A poem or any work of art is supposed to reflect the individual outlook of the artist and there is no right or wrong way to do it. It is your art from your part of view from your soul and when you feel that it is done to your satisfaction, regardless of what anyone else says about whether it is "Right" or "Wrong", then it is done correctly. If you do not feel it is right or complete, then work on it some more until YOU are satisfied with it.



</answer>

It's fine. It's a poem of your experience and feelings so no one should tell you how to write it. <question>



My feeble Partenza Represa - does it meet the criteria?



Our Neighbours (We've lived next door in a semi-detached house
For over 25 years.  During that time they have 
spoken to us about five times.....each time
it was to complain about something!  We have
never felt driven to initiate a conversation with them!)



Oy'd loike to murder me neighbours
Neighbours who've lived next door f'years.
F'r years they've ignored ar' presence.
Presents from them do not appear!

Them do not appear to loike we.
We believe likewise in return.
In return they just ignore me
Me! Off'rins of peace they just spurn

Spurn me  and Oy gets angry, see. 
See - Oy'll get me revenge on them.
Them'le be loike a humble bee
Humble before me - Oy condemn.

Oy condemn them both to 'ades.
A despicable pair they be.
They be less pop'lar than herpes
Her peskiness just gets to me.

To me they are a waste of space
Spaced-out is what they seem to be.
To be rid of both, leave no trace?
Trace fingerprints back? Not to me.

This is written in dialect because it enabled
me to cheat eg 'Them do not appear to like we'



</question>

<answer from>



Lullë Rhymesmith sonneter
Member since: 18 July 2008
Total points: 365 (Level 2)



</answer from>



<answer>



One thing to note: 
I didn't get your rhyming, If you have difficulty finding SENSIBLE rhymes, write in free verse.

Your first quatrain starts with a cliche expression and that takes away all the appeal. the first line of your seconds stanza, "In my deeply poisoned mind" does not fit with the rest of what you said...why is your mind poisoned? Change that line.

The rest of your "Poem/song thingy" Is very direct and not done with any skill or artsy. I see no poetic techniques. So I won't call this a poem. Also, your theme is very unoriginal and cliche. I suggest you change your point of view.

Good luck :)
Lulle



Source(s):



Please have a look at my poem, I hope it helps:

http://answers.yahoo.com/question/index;...



</answer>

<question>



Storm: Care to comment please?



Storm
Dawn, and the sun was peaking
Across the quiet, of the sea sleeping
The gentle rhythmic sound of the waves
Crashing against the cliff side caves.
Seagulls sounding from the rocks nearby
The sea has woken, they can hear it sigh.
Dark clouds are formed overhead,
While fish lie low, on the sea bed.
The roar of the ocean is heard from afar
As holidaymakers get back in their cars
Passing ships, retreat in dread
But the storm was unfazed it was way ahead
They didn’t have a chance, the storm, far too clever,
Condemning innocent lives, to the murky sea, forever.
Flashes of lightning, bolt from the sky
While the waves rage on, ferocious but sly,
Engulfing anything that stands in their way
Like a merciless killer attacking its prey
Soon, without warning, the dark clouds cleared
The waves lying calm, previously feared,
Wreckage of the storm, washed up on the sand
A reminder of the destruction that was unplanned.
Peace once again, dusk was creeping
Across the quiet of the sea sleeping.



</question>

<question from>



JULIA B
Member since: 05 August 2008
Total points: 96 (Level 1)



</question from>



<question>



Help identify poem and writer 1820 tombstone:



"Adieu my friends affectionate adieu
Surely there is another Lot.
there is [ _____] home for me
Where I shall rest, remembering not
The sorrow of this day.
O, [ ___] home [ ______] of rest and peace
The [  ________]
Where [ _______]
And [ ________] meet again."

This is on 6x's grandfather's tombstone and I would like to have the full poem restored.  Thank for any help!



</question>



<answer from>



ajunker2...
Member since: 07 May 2007
Total points: 10182 (Level 6)



</answer from>



<answer>



I can reconstruct part, it is from the early romantic period, after the first Great Awakening.  Biblical images abound. "O, happy home, Jerusalem of rest and peace." I'll keep working on it, and look through my sources from the period.

It has marked similarity to "Land of Rest" written by Joseph Bromehead in 1795.
The metre is irregular, unless syllables are elided.  It begins 10.8. ____(8 or 10), 9.6. (11, as reconstructed),  This is highly unlikely to be quoted from a Hymn, unless rewritten.



</answer>



<answer from>

<question>



Can any one tell me what they thing of my poem please? ?



For that’s why God sent Mommies and Daddies!
By: Stephonie Peak



Mommy may not always be fare,
Mommy we know always cares.
Mommy everyday stands up for she is right,
Mommy understands a child’s cry when the get scared.



For that’s why God gave us mommies.



Mommy always knows what we need,
 Mommy will be there when we call.
Mommy wants to hear her child’s prayers,
Mommy needs to be respected from her kids.
For that’s why God sent us mommies.

Daddy wants to protect us from all harm,
Daddy wants to heal us from our broken heart.
Daddy wants us to remain his little children, 
Daddy wants us to have a submissive heart.
For that’s why God gave us daddies.

Daddy wants to understand where we come from,
Daddy wants no one to us from him.
Daddy will help me when in trouble,
Daddy will give me a understanding heart. 
For that’s why God sent us daddies.



We may not tell them, “Thank you,”
They may be long gone for us to understand. 
Why they are willing to help us anytime,
Now we know why mommy and daddy what they did. 
For that’s why God sent us mommies and daddies.

I tried to pull you to me, needing the touch of your skin. But you were looking somewhere else, and you walked away, never looking back. <question>



Following in the footsteps of Philip Larkin. Do you like oranges?



(Don't answer the question - just read my damn poem)

Philip Larkin - TOADS
First verse his, remainder mine - no idea of his verses, so decided on free-form for continuation

Why should I let the toad work
Squat on my life?
Can't I use my wit as a pitchfork
And drive the brute off?
_______________________
He sits in malevolent silence
Overseeing my every move.
Blinking and licking his eyeballs
Intimidation his torturer's tool.
His warty compelling presence
in the dank corner of my office room
Keeps my nose to the grind-stone
Disfiguring my promising youth.

Why should I let the toad work
Squat on my life?
The alternative is life-long leisure,
idleness and sloth.
Those disgusting fat slimy slugs
mating and multiplying
inside my head.

(don't actually believe that - but was trying to convince myself)



</question>

The Toad Poems by Gerald Locklin and George Carroll a rare animal — a romantic comedy inhabited by literate and witty people. The play is based on the poems of Locklin, which are integrated seamlessly into the text. As demonstrated in the script, they examine with sly humor and perception the joys and upsets of contemporary domestic life and male-female relationships in general; there are also forays into other topics, including odes to such diverse subjects as Beethoven and beer.

<question>



From among my poems, a homey one, your comments?



The Cast Iron Skillet



The old iron skillet
Has seen many meals
And the older it gets
The better it feels
In over a century
It has often grown crust
After some washings
Shown occasional rust
But brought back to use
Being patiently seasoned
Has withstood abuse
Its surface well blackened
Polished smooth and non-sticking
By alternate cooking
Cleansing with salt
Used hot for cold meat
Simmered beans
 on low constant heat
Used for deep frying
Then for baking cornbread
Without even trying
to a smooth polish lead
Marriage s a cast iron pan
Well seasoned in constant use
It improves with age
Relation of woman and man
With good use and correction
Lasts generation to generation
A little bit of salt, 
a bit of sugar and butter
Gives meaning to life 
and keeps folks together. 
© February 10, 2008, Albert K. jungers. All Rights Reaerved



</question>



<additional details>



While it cooks quickly, an iron skillet is not for TV dinners.  Some things take and deserve time.



</additional details>

<question>



What do you think of this poem? I DIDN'T WRITE IT...



The captains daughter by James T Fields

We were crowded in the cabin,
Not a soul would dare to sleep,
It was midnight on the waters,
And a storm was on the deep.

"Tis a fearful thing in winter
To be shattered by the blast,
And to hear the rattling trumpet
Thunder, "Cut away the mast!"

So we shuddered there in silence,
For the stoutest held his breath,
While the hungry sea was roaring
And the breakers talked with Death.

As thus we sat in darkness,
Each one busy with his prayers,
"We are lost!" the captain shouted
As he staggered down the stairs.

But his little daughter whispered,
As she took his icy hand,
"Isn't God, upon the ocean,
Just the same as on the land?"

Then we kissed the little maiden.
And we spoke in better cheer,
And we anchored safe in harbour
When the morn was shining clear



</question>

<question>



What do you think of this poem by Whitman?



When I heard the learn'd astronomer;
When the proofs, the figures, were ranged in columns before me;
When I was shown the charts and the diagrams, to add, divide, and



measure them;
When I, sitting, heard the astronomer, where he lectured with much



applause in the lecture-room,
How soon, unaccountable, I became tired and sick;
Till rising and gliding out, I wander'd off by myself,
In the mystical moist night-air, and from time to time,
Look'd up in perfect silence at the stars.

<question from>

<question>



For lovers of the mystic poem, your comments?



JOURNEY



At the Garden's Centre, two trees stood
The journey of a lifetime goes from wood to wood.
Always too easy, saints of later day
Parents second guess, their faults gainsay. 
As if, by means  of grace to them unowned 
We, of ourselves, their fate descry;
Its doom escape, forbear to die, unscathed triumphant
And with battle cry the Serpent trammel, undo his rant.
In righteous indignation adjudge the Source of life,
Call 'uncleanness' blood, and labour's worthy strife
Just due for her duplicitous part
Held less than Man as if wrought by his art 
Though in pain She gives birth.
So the Journey begins,
The story of our worth
The Record of our sins.

Onward now it winds through courses yet unknown,
Leaves  of wrath fall from the tree further to be blown,
Bitterness of the life's sap that sapped from us our life.
We thirst yet for another wherein lifesap yet doth flow;
Wholesome Tree  where we may taste and grow.
Another Adam at that Tree stands
Arms outstretched with open hands,
Receiving the fruit bitter found when we did test and eat.
Another Eve stands thereby, serpent 'neath her feet.
They call us yet to be Create,
For we are but Dust before
That Moistness and the Breath
Giving life where lore
Taught us nought but death,
At the Centre of the Garden
The Place of Adam's skull.

In pride Iblis disdained to bow 
Would then he'd known the How
By Woman he should be undone
 His wrath the method wherein Journey's end
 Should at the last be won
 At the Centre of the Garden two trees stand.



© December 30, 2007 Albert K. Jungers  All rights reserved



</question>



<additional details>



Iblis corresponds to Satan in the Qu'ran's telling of the story.



</additional details>



<answer from>

Member since: 19 June 2008
Total points: 2563 (Level 4)

Contributing In:

<answer>



You have a great beginning. I've broken it into short lines -- they usually catch your readers imagination.



The first thing you do when you finish getting your poem ready for posting (or submitting to a publisher) is to run a spell checker. YA says there are 6 misspellings in the copy / paste of your poem.  You can see what you would have saved.  Also, never write a poem with the text spelling, it will always mark you as an amateur. Also capitalize I when used in a documetn, unless you wish to become another e.e.commings..

This has gorgeous imagery.



Your beAuty rises (Misspelled)
above the sight 
of a thousand roses 
gleaming in a 
golden light on a 
crISp spring morning &lt;-- transposed

Your warmth resembles a sun kissed cheek

Though I might never

<answer>



First of all, if you're 14 and have a desire to write poetry, then you're more mature and in touch with your soul than most your age.  That being said, you need to understand that poetry is like painting...only you're using words to create images instead of colored oils.  So, if you painted a picture, but used the wrong colors, or failed to stay within the lines, then asked someone what they thought...well, they might not tell you the obvious things like "you didn't stay between the lines and you used the wrong colors"...but they'd miss the fact that you even "wanted" to paint!  So...when you write "odl" instead of "old", or "beuty" instead of "beauty", you're not staying inside the lines...but it's so easy to correct misspellings...just use your spellchecker, and if yours is broken, then use a dictionary.  It may seem picky, but imagine someone running into a theater and yelling, "you have to leave because the building is on fir!"...people would start laughing...and get burned up in the process.  This is what I'm talking about: distraction.  Yes, we know what words you "meant" to write, but when we stumble over a misspelled word, we stop reading for a second...and that takes us off the flow.  So...fix the spelling...it's easy to do and will pay dividends.  The good news is that although some may consider your images cliche, you're too young to have heard them enough for them to be cliche, so it means you probably thought them up yourself...so for you, they were not cliche...and they are some really good images.

So, seeing many, many poems written by others your age, I would say that although you need to work on your spelling, your image creation (which is very, very important in poetry) is better than average and I sense you have a kind heart.  Also, you don't need to tell us you're not gay...just because you write poetry does not mean you're gay...and those of us a bit older understand that...in fact, anyone on this part of YA knows that by default :)

Don't let my comments discourage you...in fact, I hope they "encourage" you to write more, because it's obvious you have desire...and it will help you become a better writer, and a better speaker...poetry does that to people...so keep writing.



Source(s):



Editor, New Poets Press



</answer>

<question>



Long poem I wrote today; any good?



Be Positive...

They feed us with pills
When we don't even ask
They help our ills
Get well is the task
We don't fit in
Medication stops strife
They say it is us
Something wrong with our life

But what if it's them
And their messed up society
Drunken weekends
Hardly ever sobriety
Heavy work week
With partners they seek
A slice of the pie
They try not to cry

And questions may rise
In their love-struck eyes
Isn't something missing
That thought soon replaced
By dating and kissing

As long as the cogs of machinery turn
All must be well
Nothing else need they learn

The spirit suppressed
By material gain
Anything else could be seen as insane
Unless they become us
And their friends whom they trust
Turn away and declare
With an absent stare
You are not well
Go straight to Hell

So now you are us
Sell the car
Catch the bus
Forget your lover 
She won't understand
No longer will you hold her hand

Get ready for despair
And people who don't care
Loneliness is home for you
Just what on earth is one to do

The world will change
As far as you know
Your old friend
May become your foe

How can one cope 
While poisoned with dope
Legal highs
Heavy sighs
Broken keys
Hateful enemies

The best thing, I say, trust in God
Whether Teddy Rocker Punk or Mod
Or something else
There are so many
Just don't get killed like Kenny

There's another life
Apart from this one
It's spiritual and perfect
With a blazing sun
Never to set
Unless you wish so
Sometimes stars shine
With the sun low

It waits for you
While you are awake
You get there by sleeping
This dream's not a fake
Hope is it's name
There are others too
No one is old
Everything is new

There are no adults
Only children who play
There is no danger
Nothing evil to say
There is no school
For that makes you grow
All is cool 
With nothing to know

So good luck for your plight
Wrong or right
Material or not
Even world forgot

All I ask is that one day you'll remember
The place with no September
No fall
No crowded shopping mall
No paranoia in paradise
No naughty
Just nice



</question>

<answer>



Since your poem has a cadence, beats matter:

Some say I should be published
Some say I should be damned
One'd like to see my manuscript
Firmly up my backside rammed

This would keep your beats the same without changing the first three lines (other than the contraction "one'd" for "one would"), and invert the word order in line four so the anapaestic start mirrored line three's new beginning beat (changed from Trochee to Anapaest by the contraction) and would quickly move you through your final line.

hope this helps



Source(s):



Editor, New Poets Press



</answer>

The Spell.

<answer>



Concept...I'd give you a "7"...execution, a "5".  Tighten it up...try to say the same thing with less...create more images and do less telling...try to set up situations where "we" come to the same conclusions...instead of just telling us what we should think...and remember that not everyone who fights a war wanted to have a war in the first place...some just didn't want to speak German and wear a swastika.



Source(s):



Editor, New Poets Press



</answer>

<question>



Relative truth: a new poem would you please comment on it



Truth begins with a little white lie
Ask the vicar, the priest or the rev
They never give answers for the truth that you seek
They give answers from books in its stead

The words that are written
Sins all done forgiven
a Gospel truth  made up in dread
For eyes with closed minds
They follow the lines
Of the truth passed to them by the dead

Truth means something to someone
But truth differs from home to home
No-one will listen to the truth you share
Too wrapped up in truth of their own

Truth is relative to the life we live
Our presuppositions take hold
We pass them on to the next generation
So they live by the truth we have told

Thus begins a vicious life’s circle
Of which an end is no-where in sight
For the truth that pushed us to find it
Has been lost in the glare of false light



(Copyright © Geoffrey Brett  02/08/2008)



</question>



<additional details>



Atheists, Christians, Muslims, etcetc
we all live by different truths.



http://www.poetrybysilvertongue.com/



</additional details>

<question>



My poem - advice please?



I had to write a poem for my English anthology assignment and this is what it ended up being. Can anyone give me some advice, I feel like something is wrong or missing. Btw Im 14 and this is like my first poem =)

So I Keep Running - By CR

I keep running, 
And no one comes to catch me
There’s no one waiting for me to come back,

<answer from>



BT Jeppesen
Member since: 18 September 2008
Total points: 115 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Hey CR,

This is an impressive poem for both a 14-year-old and a first-time poet.  I have a few minor suggestions, and one major.

First, I would suggest shortening the title to just Keep Running.  I have never liked the use of simple words like "So" and "I" in titles.

Okay, my big suggestion is concerning what you think is missing.  I do feel like something is missing.  This poem could easily be made longer.  I have this picture of you running, and I understand that there is no one coming after you because there is no one who really cares to.  But that's it.  While it is a good image, it could be drastically improved.  Instead, show you running, don't just say that you are running.  Then show what your family or whoever is doing.  Show them not caring that you have disappeared.  Show, don't tell.  That is the most important thing to remember in all creative writing.  Let me just show you an example of how this poem could be shown with images to be improved:

Through heated breeze and murky sweat, I run,
and am surprised at my isolation,
while at home, tossing popcorn in mouths,
they sit, unaware that I have left.

Of course, I won't complain if you use what I put there, but you did such a good job on the first version that I think you'd have more fun rewriting the poem yourself using my suggestions.  I am sincere in saying this was a good poem.  Based solely on this, I think you might be able to do well as a poet if you worked at it.  If you'd like, you may send me an email or IM me when you have an updated version.  I'd be happy to take another look and give more suggestions.  You can contact me through this site.



</answer>



<answer from>

<question>



Anyone like to comment on my new poem or suggest a title? Thanks :)?



In anticipation of the time
When leaves crunch underfoot
Audibly satisfying,
Flame-hued, burnished gold,
I kick them out of my way.

As I smile with nostalgia and remember,
Last autumn;
My erstwhile lover, whose idea of romance –
Was not asking what I wanted, but was going to the bar
And getting the drinks in unprompted.

In anticipation of the time
When frost lies underfoot,
Blue-tinged and pretty,
Waiting for me to lose concentration,
And land on my rear.

As I shake my head slowly, and look back upon,
Last winter;
My bygone lover, whose idea of affection – 
Was pointing out his mothers grey hairs
Before yanking them out.

In anticipation of the time
When spring will arrive,
And it will pass,
Followed by summer,
This will pass also.

And I’ll be here again,
Where I am now,
And without any trace of sadness,
I’ll laugh without the accompanying dull ache,
At my bittersweet memories
Of my erstwhile, bygone and ill-suited lover.



</question>



<additional details>



Of course he had some redeeming features! I do look back on it fondly and the poem was never intended to be nasty - more a recognition of how ill-suited we were :)



</additional details>

<question>



Work and play by ted hughes?



im writing a critical essay on the poem work and play by ted hughes but im finding it difficult to summarise what the poem is about and set out a good introduction for it. Can anyone give me any help or advice it will be much appreciated.
thanks a lot!x



</question>



</answer from>



<answer>



This poem is about a comparison between a swallow and human beings that are on a day trip. The swallow, is at work in the poem and is feeling content. The humans, however, are supposed to be relaxing and having fun, but they feel miserable instead. With this, there is irony here with the title, as the swallow is working but having fun. The writer, I feel, is being biased in his poem. He tends to be in favour of the swallow. The poem is describing the people as 'polluting' the environment. The message of the poem is that we shouldn't destroy our environment and our health by 'baking' ourselves under the sun. The poem talks about the tourists arriving and then leaving unhappily. The writer is also describing the swallow's day, what it does to entertain itself and returning...♥



Source(s):



http://www.coursework.info/AS_and_A_Leve...



</answer>

<answer>



Example Of Descriptive Essays



Billy Ray's Pawn Shop and Lawn Mower Repair looked like a burial ground for country auction rejects. The blazing, red, diesel fuel tanks beamed in front of the station, looking like cheap lipstick against the pallid, wrinkled texture of the parking lot sand. The yard, not much larger than the end zone at General G. Patton High School on the north end of town, was framed with a rusted metallic hedge of lawn mowers, banana seat bicycles, and corroded oil drums. It wasn't a calico frame of rusted parts, but rather an orchestra of unwanted machinery that Billy Ray had arranged into sections. The yellow-tanked mowers rested silently at the right of the diesel fuel. Once red, now faded orange, mowers stood at attention to the left. The oil barrels, jaded and pierced with holes, bellared like chimes when the wind was right. The bikes rested sporadically throughout the lot. In the middle of it all was the office, a faded, steel roof supported by cheap two-by-fours and zebra paneling. Billy..



Source(s):



Frat Files



</answer>

<answer>



I think 'At Grass' by Philip Larkin is quite a descriptive poem aswell as having a very important underlying theme regarding how our society rejects the elderly.



The eye can hardly pick them out 
From the cold shade they shelter in, 
Till wind distresses tail and mane; 
Then one crops grass, and moves about 
- The other seeming to look on - 
And stands anonymous again



Yet fifteen years ago, perhaps 
Two dozen distances sufficed 
To fable them : faint afternoons 
Of Cups and Stakes and Handicaps, 
Whereby their names were artificed 
To inlay faded, classic Junes -



Silks at the start : against the sky 
Numbers and parasols : outside, 
Squadrons of empty cars, and heat, 
And littered grass : then the long cry 
Hanging unhushed till it subside 
To stop-press columns on the street.



Do memories plague their ears like flies? 
They shake their heads. Dusk brims the shadows. 
Summer by summer all stole away, 
The starting-gates, the crowd and cries - 
All but the unmolesting meadows. 
Almanacked, their names live; they



Have slipped their names, and stand at ease, 
Or gallop for what must be joy, 
And not a fieldglass sees them home, 
Or curious stop-watch prophesies : 
Only the grooms, and the groom's boy, 
With bridles in the evening come.



</answer>

<question>



Would you like to reread my poem about Autumn?



Autumn

Autumn (again).

My favourite time of
the year. Which is
rather perverse now
that I come to think
about it, because
'The Fall' (as our
Yankee and Canadian
cousins insist on calling
it) is all about death
and decay.

Withered leaves
falling from branches,
grass which is parched
and dry.
Colours of brown
and red and gold
against a backdrop
of grey sky.

However, all this
degeneration is but a
prelude to when the earth
will live again -
recuscitated, regenerated,
reborn. Everything
regrows. Reincarnation,
I suppose.

Except that I
don't believe in that
particular philosophy.

(Although I used to when
I was a giraffe.)



</question>



<answer from>

Robert Harrison
Member since: 20 November 2007
Total points: 1831 (Level 3)

<answer>



Adam,
You have written a charming poem here. It is not meant to be read, but the idea is to listen to you reading it; which is what I did. What made this possible were your last five lines, and then have you read the whole poem to me.

I close by saying (With a cheeky grin upon my face) with all due respect to you as a good poet, but one who is also as "Nutty as a fruit cake", and "A suitable case for treatment"

Robert



</answer>

<question>



Is this poem-like story in English—funny?



WHATEVER YOU DO, DON’T
ANSWER BACK



The clank-banging? Ignore it.
She’s looking for the coffee and 
her magic wand…the one that smokes
from one end.

“What the Heaven!”
“Decaf!”
“What good is a gun that ain’t loaded!?!”



Fairy Queens are hard to manage, especially
the unmanageable ones…and my poor kitchen,

“Half & Half!”
“You want my butt to go enormous!?!”

Give her a job, like some Shakespeare to cook down,
in the big stock pot, too heavy for her to lift.

That way she can only sit and watch it bubble…

*****



</question>

<question>



First attempt at an acrostic, let me know if it makes sense ?



Sand too warm by noon
Umber shades of shadow
Rollers now quite low
Foam dancin’ about

Frantic gulls swoopin’ cry
Infernal glare seekin’ my eye
Shufflin’ along sands deep
Headin’ on for the surf
In water standin’ knee high
Nothin’ more relaxin’ 
Gonna go fishin’

Bobber snatched from sight
Attacked from just below
I’m studyin’, ponderin' the line
Tension now increasin’

Reel whirlin’, blindin’ fast
Only thing to do, hangin’ on
Backin’ up, nothin’ gained
Bait done been stripped
Ever so cleanly, sigh, yet again
Reelin’ in, castin’ one more time.



Any and all comments and suggestions are, as always, appreciated.



</question>

<question from>



★Mrs. Edward Cullen★
Member since: 30 November 2006
Total points: 10544 (Level 6)



</question from>



<question>



Why you think writers would use literary devices and rhythm patterns?



why you think writers would use literary devices and rhythm patterns.



How does having an understanding of these devices affect your understanding of the lyrics?



</question>



<answer from>



traveling supervisor
Member since: 19 July 2008
Total points: 5024 (Level 5)



</answer from>



<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



Literary devices and rhythm patters set the poets apart from the prose authors and presents a style that, when done well, conveys a clear meaning in far fewer words.



For sure, poetry can be penned without regard to devices and rhythm, it quite often is; then it feels and reads more like a dairy entry or thoughts expressed jumbled and tumbled as they often are when first acknowledged in our minds.

Brevity with concise expression is the hallmark of a really good poet.



The second part of the question is not as simple to explain,,, perhaps I could best sum it up this way with an example from one of my poems.

If you understand the concepts of how a poem is constructed, then you understand that you are not seeing all the details the poet saw when they wrote the verse.  Your imagination comes into play with a poem, as you, the reader, are left to fluff out the details offered within the poem to suit your experiences.

Here is a small bit of verse with two words per line that capture the essence of what I had experienced at the beach, however, I want you as the reader to relate with what I am describing, not merely absorb every detail I could have offered.

Sun blazed
colors paled
Tanned bodies
skittle suits

Warm sands
time chills
Memory flickers 
darkness calls

Night illuminated
lighthouse winked 
Visual reminder
footsteps past

This may not be the best example, but it is what I have available.

Hopefully this long winded reply helps.



</answer>

Emily Dickison Poetry Help Please..x =[?



It can't be "Summer"!
That — got through!
It's early — yet — for "Spring"!

Before the Blackbirds sing!

haroldpo...

</answer from>



<answer>



I think that she was looking at the western sky in late evening and musing about the colors she saw. She questions what the colors signify and discards in turn that they might be related to summer, spring or winter. Then, as she had a tendency to do, she thought of death, and wondered if it could be death they signified, but decided that white, not the reddish color she saw, would signify death. Then, I think, while she was still musing, the sunset ended the display of color and the sky turned opalescent - the color and transparency of chrysolite gemstones - and not too far from white.

Be assured that the above is strictly guesswork and represents no scholarly understanding.



</answer>



<answer from>



rusty
Member since: 16 September 2008
Total points: 170 (Level 1)



</answer from>



<answer>



Dickinson using the seasons as a metaphor for the stages of life. Spring represents youth; summer represents adulthood. Fall or "Rouge" represents old age, and "White" is a representation of winter, or dying. By the way, the seasons are often used in this way by many other poets as well.

In this poem, Dickinson can't believe that summer is already over, because that means that spring is not next. It means that winter (dying) is not here because it it not yet "white, " and therefore the blackbirds (death) have not come yet either. All of this leaves her with autumn, with "rouge" and "sunset" representing the fall colors. The sunset also symbolizes the impending ending of life.

Overall, the theme is that the speaker is shocked by  how quickly the seasons change, and thus how quickly life is passing leaving her facing the inevitability that death will be coming sooner rather than later. The poem ends by returning to spring and 'Cuffs of Chrysolite!' which signifies the circle of life, a recurring theme in Dickinson's poetry.



</answer>

<answer>



Oppenheim's Cup and Saucer by Carol Ann Duffy 
She asked me to luncheon in fur. Far from
the loud laughter of men, our secret life stirred.

I remember her eyes, the slim rope of her spine.
This is your cup, she whispered, and this mine.

We drank the sweet hot liquid and talked dirty.
As she undressed me, her breasts were a mirror

and there were mirrors in the bed. She said Place
your legs around my neck, that's right. Yes.

do this one it is sick, ur teacher will be shocked



Source(s):



http://frombooksofpoems.blogspot.com/



</answer>



<answer from>



Diana P
Member since: 13 June 2007
Total points: 17650 (Level 6)

<answer>



Read the first line which is grammatically wrong.
So many have GONE through this type of pain or So many WENT - not "have went".
And those who say grammar isn't important because it's only a way of expressing yourself, are right if the poem is for the author's eyes only.  As soon as he offers it to public scrutiny he owes it to himself and his audience to check it.

<question>



Another one from me, critique, constructive feedback?



I'm not actually sure I want to actually look for feedback on this, basically due to the fact I like it even though I'm aware of a few flaws that I'm going to try and iron out! But really I want to know what you think on the rough draft level!



Transient



Crystal echoes, magnolia sky,
Bury whispers, in bright burning eyes
Nocturnal torments of loving cries
Re-run the moments in endless flash backs of sight
Visit, Re-visit, Visit, and Re-visit the static you shed
Claw back, the waltz that we shared in transient misery gloom
Declare love the victory, as the Rose I bought you withers burns
Wade in the water of the fountain that you paved
Answer the telephone as it rings, go on ostracize my name
Never mind, beg, plead I have no desire to be saved
It’s a bittersweet game, Russian roulette leave it up to me to take blame

Please if your feedback is of a destructive tone, I don't want to hear because while it may be an attack only on the poem I take it as an attack on myself!



</question>



<additional details>



I have to say that it was never my intention to write a love poem, with it being pointed out to me I can definitely see that is what it seems to be speaking of, but as stupid/pompous as this might come across when I write I just put words down I don't even really think of them further than liking the way they sound when I read them to myself



</additional details>

<answer>



Unrequited love blames no one...not even the players. This is too much written goodness to really critique...you have plenty of concrete imagery...but on the parts that don't...revise them and let the reader see what you are saying....take out the unneccessary words...and the meaning will remain the same...yes, it will!

Write onwards...do NOT let critiques dull your pen!!!

<question>



Can you think of a title for my poem?



I need a catchy title for my poem



It’s that time of the year,
When families and relatives shed a tear,
As they remember the ones they have lost,
In the bloody war that took the lives of thousands Canadian soldiers.
The brave soldiers spent their life in fear and pain,
For the freedom and peace we would gain.
We honour the lives of the veterans,
As we live our lives,
Under the blanket of freedom,
Provided by them.
The poppies people around the country wear,
Show that people like me and you still care.
We gather and open our hearts to share,
A great moment of silence as we say a prayer.
Remember those valiant soldiers who fought before,
And the ones who are still at war.
In our hearts they will always stay,
In this honourable Remembrance Day.



As the national anthem plays,
Sing clear and loud
While you wear you poppies with pride.
As you can see,
Because of them, you and I are free.



We own a thank you to those who stood brave and tall
Who fought and died for one and all.



</question>

<question from>



Wylie Nelson
Member since: 15 May 2008
Total points: 1125 (Level 3)



</question from>



<question>



What say you to a poem inspired by song lyrics?



She is Gone, by Willie Nelson
(lyrics and link follow)



She is gone but she was here



and her presence is still heavy in the air
What a taste of human love



now she's gone



and it don't matter anymore
Crossing dreams with our lives



it was more than just a woman and a man
It was love without the sky



now my life will never be the same again



http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=R3IZupZ40...



A little happier version, perhaps?



You are Here



You are here, I know you're near
as I feel your hands caress my hair with love
your kiss I taste from up above
you're not gone
what we were matters still my dear
we lived our dreams in full delight
it was more than a husband and a wife
it was us, we did not want
and now I wait to be with you once again.



</question>

<answer>



<evaluation>Best Answer - Chosen by Asker</evaluation>



I liked your take on the song.
It does bring a fresher and  happier tone.
I like to be inspired by songs as well, but copying a thought someone else has had, to me is not being the creative person you are.
Making up a new poem based on your thoughts and emotions of the song could have presented something  quite astonishing for us to read.....



</answer>



<asker's comment>



You are right, it was a poor idea, I confess and won't do it again!



</asker's comment>

<answer>



While in my opinion one could never improve upon the original,
I will agree that your version is a happier one,
but perhaps one the song writer himself could not feel.



It's a beautiful song nonetheless.
